Current Commentary

The Japanese Army's Withdrawal from Luandong and Our Country's Countermeasures (Part 2) – Ming 26

The Conversion of Policy Towards Japan

The Japanese militarists, aware of the internal and external situations, deeply understand that prolonging the war is not a good strategy. Therefore, they have changed their tactics, concealing their military weaknesses, and simultaneously not using their weaknesses to attack our country's strengths. Our army indeed lacks modern equipment, and three-dimensional warfare is not something we are accustomed to. The only option is a final decisive battle. The infantry's weapons, in well-trained units, can exert their sniping effectiveness and demonstrate their characteristics of fighting independently. If the Japanese army recklessly advances, without our preparation for a total mobilization along the entire line, it will indeed be difficult to secure victory. However, it is also certain that Japan will not be able to peacefully occupy the entire territory of Rehe as it did before. Therefore, the Japanese army wants to obtain the greatest reward with the smallest sacrifice. The only option is to withdraw the Japanese troops from Luandong and concentrate their forces on another point to attack our side. Furthermore, while the Japanese troops in Luandong are pretending to retreat, they are attacking Nanti’anmen quite urgently. One reason is to observe whether our country's military internal affairs are well-organized. Another reason is to falsely prove that their empty talk of defending the Great Wall is not a lie, in order to deceive international public opinion and fool their own people. Therefore, they can use a smaller force to restrain our huge forces along the Luan River up to Gubeikou, and be able to draw elite troops to attack Zhangduo.

The situation within Chahar is not as dangerous as Rehe, and it lacks elite troops capable of fighting. Sun Dianying's unit has traveled thousands of miles, but occupying and holding territory is not its strength. The Shanxi army under Fu Zuoyi has shown merit in internal affairs, but they are also small-scale battles. They not only lack a correct and clear understanding of international warfare, but they also probably lack a thorough and concrete understanding of the Japanese imperialists who are the enemies in front of them. Using them to fight against Japan, how can we expect them to win?

Indeed, in the current situation, our country is forced into an inferior position, which is undeniable and should not be denied. However, our people are the most hardworking and diligent in the world, and our reserves of coal, iron, and oil are second only to North America. Using this to fight against Japan, there is no reason why we cannot save ourselves. Moreover, the final victory or defeat of modern warfare does not lie in the current military equipment, but in the economic strength of the country. Since the outbreak of the global economic panic, Japan's national strength has been declining day by day. More than half of the rural population is almost entirely trapped in the tragic state of living in difficulty. However, its warlords are using foreign military operations to cover up their ugliness. If our country can truly fight to the death with them, then the right to settle the final victory or defeat will ultimately be in our hands. Therefore, although our military strength is weak, if we can strive to hold on, there will definitely be a day to turn defeat into victory. However, where does the path to victory lie? Where does the path to our self-salvation lie?

First, we must launch a nationwide national struggle. Our country has been weak for a long time, and our ingrained habits are too deep. Without intense stimulation, it will be difficult to overcome the inertia passed down from history. Recently, the three northeastern provinces have been forcibly seized, and the Rehe area has been further ravaged. The five counties of Luandong are almost entirely under the threat of enemy forces. Enemy cavalry have been seen in many important passes along the Great Wall. These events not only affect politics, but also directly threaten the daily lives of individuals. Young people with warm blood have long been filled with resentment and eagerness to vent it. Even those who are gentle and prudent are thinking about how to serve the country and be loyal to the nation. For the current plan, it is appropriate to mobilize the entire Chinese nation and launch this extraordinary situation. Regardless of temporary success or failure, we must determine the fundamental strategy for fighting against Japan, and then the precarious situation can be opened up.

Second, we must actively cultivate the rural economy and control the urban economy. The main reason for our country's weakness is that politics is not on the right track, but is merely a contradiction in the upper-level structure. In fact, the fundamental ingrained problem lies in the decline of the agricultural economy. Commercial capital has no possibility of transforming into a purely capitalist economic organization, and a new path has not yet been opened up. Therefore, it is subject to extreme pressure from the commodities and financial capital of various countries, and internally it is oppressed by the unreasonable ravages of warlords. The axis of conversion from now on is cultivating rural production, which is essential. Revolving rural finance is also necessary. Moreover, illegal suppression and unreasonable exploitation, as well as general exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies, must be immediately exempted. Corvée labor and requisitions should be strictly prohibited. Otherwise, the destruction of the countryside will become even more unbearable, and the crisis of the nation's future will be further intensified. Most of the general urban (economy) is engaged in commercial transshipment, with fewer centered on industry. However, there are also some regions that have the rudiments of modern industry. At this time of unfolding an extraordinary situation, the first thing to do is to have a detailed and thorough investigation. The second thing to do is to make the various industrial organizations prepared for extraordinary times. The third thing to do is to prepare for wartime control. Only then can we concentrate our national strength to fight a long-term battle with the enemy.

Third, politics in extraordinary times must be based on the masses. Our country has a vast territory, and transportation is inconvenient. It is indeed not easy to get the masses of the whole country to participate in politics. However, we must not give up eating because of choking, ignoring the power of the masses. For example, the Japanese warlords, although acting willfully, must always borrow the masses as a premise, using (the veterans' association) as the backbone to inspire their citizens and incite their aggressive ambitions. Otherwise, they will still not be able to avoid failure. Moreover, since the Northern Expedition unified our country, political thought has become increasingly developed. With a great enemy at hand, if there is no mass base in politics, there will be no way out internally, and what can be done externally? Therefore, the opening up of political power is naturally a matter of course. In particular, it is necessary to safeguard the interests of the hardworking masses in order to achieve the effect of cooperation between the upper and lower levels and to live up to the reality of national unity.

The above three points are indeed abstract principles, but they are the minimum requirements for the people of our country today, and they are also the necessary conditions for fighting against Japan. We offer our foolish sincerity, hoping that the masses of our whole country will work together to break through the current difficulties and straighten the front line against Japan.

The Washington Talks Conclude

Herriot Leaves America and Returns to France 27

Joint Communiqué Issued by Roosevelt and Herriot

Practical Understanding Reached on Economic Difficulties

Establishing a Foundation for Compromise at the London Conference

(Washington) After their final talks today, President Roosevelt and French representative Herriot jointly issued a statement saying that both sides had engaged in friendly and lengthy discussions regarding the war debt issue. The purpose of the discussions was to establish a clearer and more practical understanding and to determine future steps that could be taken. Both sides hope that after Herriot reports to his government, talks will continue between Washington and Paris. A concrete compromise is expected to be reached at the World Economic Conference in June. In addition to war debts, the U.S. President and the French representative also studied the development of commercial policies to promote international trade, as well as unifying national banking policies, methods for governments to undertake public works to prevent business stagnation, and proposals to improve the silver standard. After the statement was released, Herriot departed for New York to board a ship back to France. (Reuter, 28th)

(Paris) The Paris Morning News's Washington correspondent reported briefly today on the results of the three-hour consultation between former French Premier Herriot and U.S. President Roosevelt: (1) The United States and France will declare a tariff truce from April 29 until the convening of the World Economic Conference. (2) The disposition of war debts should be handled within the general scope of the economic conference. (3) The United States is prepared to participate in a permanent, automatic international joint control of armaments. (4) In the quantitative disarmament issue, the United States is strongly opposed to the model system used by certain countries. (5) The United States intends to send observers to any conference related to the Kellogg-Briand Pact. (National Telegram, 28th)

Reciprocity and Fond Farewell 28

(Washington) This morning, French representative and former Premier Herriot paid his final visit to President Roosevelt. Herriot presented the U.S. President with a commemorative album of the Allied nations during the European War, which included photocopies of signatures of key military and political figures from various countries during the war. Roosevelt, in return, inscribed a personal photograph and presented it to Herriot to express his gratitude. As Herriot left the White House, he declared to reporters, "The United States is known to the world for its Declaration of Independence, and France's Declaration of the Rights of Man also shines in history. It is truly necessary for both nations to join hands." Herriot shook hands with Roosevelt and his wife at 11:15 a.m., both radiating vitality. They exchanged wishes for each other's well-being. As Herriot entered his car, a crowd in the White House garden surrounded him, cheering loudly, creating a feeling of fond farewell. (Havas, 28th)

Amendments to the Pact of Non-Aggression are Necessary 29

(New York) French representative and former Premier Herriot, French Ambassador to the United States de Laboulaye, and their delegation arrived here at 5:00 p.m. by special train. Herriot then made a statement to reporters, saying that he had discussed an economic truce between France and the United States with President Roosevelt. However, the duration and implementation of the truce still need further study. He hopes the economic truce can be extended at least until the London Economic Conference is convened. Subsequently, he discussed tariffs, disarmament, and security issues. Herriot said that Roosevelt's intention to improve the Briand-Kellogg Pact was admirable. The treaty does indeed require improvement and greater clarity. Herriot concluded by saying that he was very optimistic about leaving the United States and that the talks went very well. (Havas, 28th)

U.S. to Propose Tariff Truce 30

Monetary Truce Soon to Be Implemented 31

(New York) According to today's New York Times, U.S. President Roosevelt, British Prime Minister MacDonald, and French representative Herriot have agreed on a temporary monetary truce, and Germany and other countries will be invited to join. It is said that this measure will be implemented simultaneously with the tariff truce before the convening of the World Economic Conference. The pound and the dollar will be fixed at an average market price for several months. At the same time, the British economic experts who came to the United States with the British Prime Minister are now staying in the United States to observe the impact of all expansion plans. (Reuter, 29th)

Thorough Study of Silver Price Issue 32

(New York) The New York Times's Washington dispatch today stated that the silver price stipulated in the Pittman plan differs by 30% from the current silver price. Debtor nations could benefit from this, but to what extent other countries besides Britain will take advantage of this opportunity is highly speculative. Silver proponents believe that debtor nations using silver to repay debts can absorb the surplus silver in the market, gradually raising the price of silver. If Britain does not use the silver it has stockpiled in India to repay war debts, the price of silver will rise to a level detrimental to the United States. However, if Britain uses Indian silver, it can help sell it off with minimal losses, and both Britain and India will benefit if it is shipped and sold at a special price. The Indian treasury holds approximately 400 to 500 million ounces of silver, which is the main reason for the recent decline in silver prices. Congressional silver proponents expect the Pittman plan to raise the world silver price to 50 or 60 cents. It is said that India is now preparing to pay off its debt to Britain with 75 million yuan in silver. If so, Britain and India can use this to offset the war debt owed to the United States in June, with a surplus remaining. In addition to allowing debtor nations to use silver to repay debts, the United States also advocates using silver as part of the reserve for national banks and minting more silver coins. Experts from the United States, Britain, and France have thoroughly studied this proposal in London, and the suggestion to use silver to pay for various small-denomination currencies, with a maximum silver equivalent of 5 U.S. dollars, 1 British pound, or 50 or 100 French francs, is said to have been successfully resolved. However, in reality, experts from Britain and France do not seem entirely enthusiastic about the entire American plan. According to congressional leaders, Britain and France are doing this to postpone further consideration of war debts until after the World Economic Conference. (Reuter, 28th)

Undersecretary of State for Economic Affairs Moley and Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee Pittman are at the top of the list. (Havas, 28th)

U.S. Senate Finally Passes the Entire Inflation Bill 34

Rural Relief Bill Passed Simultaneously

Authorizing the President to Reduce the Gold Content of the Dollar

Issuance of New Securities and Free Minting of Silver Coins

Limit of 200 Million Yuan for Using Silver to Repay Debts

(Washington) The U.S. Senate today passed the inflation bill and the rural relief bill by an overwhelming majority, rejecting the Republican proposal to pay veterans' bonuses in cash. The two bills have now been sent to the House of Representatives, and Speaker Rayburn has guaranteed that they will pass. If the House does not amend the contents of the two bills, the U.S. President will have unlimited discretionary power over monetary policy. This inflation bill was drafted by government-appointed Senator Thomas Elmer, according to the President's intentions, and supported by John Thomas, as a supplement to the rural relief bill, to avoid the inflation faction enacting untimely legislation. Its main provisions are as follows:

(1) Authorizing the President to issue new Treasury bonds totaling 60 billion yuan.

(2) Debtor nations of war debts may repay war debts with 200 million yuan in silver within the next six months.

(3) The President may reset the value of the U.S. dollar, reducing its gold content by up to 50%.

After the Senate convened today, it proceeded with this bill. First, Johnson's motion was passed by a vote of 53 to 32, allowing debtor nations to pay with silver. The difference between the yes and no votes in today's votes was the smallest, indicating the number of people in Congress who oppose making concessions to debtor nations. Next, Senator Robinson's proposal to pay veterans' bonuses in cash, which was also considered a supplement to the rural relief bill, was rejected by a vote of 61 to 29. Then, the entire inflation bill was passed by a vote of 64 to 21. Shortly thereafter, the Senate also passed the rural relief bill by a vote of 64 to 20. At the same time, the House also passed the Home Owners' Loan Act, which allows the government to set up an agency to accept mortgages from small homeowners, protecting them from being forced into foreclosure. (National Telegram, 28th)

Contents of the Rural Relief Bill 35

The Government Will Use Extraordinary Measures

To Raise the Market Price of Basic Agricultural Products

(Washington) Since the U.S. Senate passed the rural relief bill by a vote of 64 to 20 today, the United States will begin using extraordinary measures to attempt to reduce the surplus of cotton and raise its market price. Although the bill authorizes the Department of Agriculture to find ways to reduce the acreage planted and raise the market price of all basic agricultural products, cotton will be the first to be rescued, followed by wheat, and then cattle, pigs, rice, sugar, dairy products, and tobacco. The most significant observation is that this bill will make the U.S. government a cotton merchant and tenant of raw fields. The initiators of this bill claimed today that if the opinions stipulated in the bill are implemented, the world price of cotton will have hope of rising. The main points of the bill are as follows: (1) If farmers reduce their acreage by more than 30%, the government will provide subsidies. (2) Cotton planters can reduce their plantable acreage and purchase cheap trading privileges from the Department of Agriculture (i.e., special rights to compel the other party to perform the contract of buying and selling at a fixed price at any time within a specified period), the quantity of which is equal to the amount reduced in comparison with the previous year's harvest. (3) The government will lease the boundary land of farmers' fields to create forests or other uses that do not compete with farmers. (4) The government may accept rural mortgages through land banks and special financial institutions and provide long-term, low-interest loans. (5) The Department of Agriculture may stipulate the minimum price at which agricultural products are sold in the domestic market and guarantee the maintenance of this price. (6) The government may levy taxes on the buying and selling of basic agricultural products, using the tax revenue to fund acreage reduction subsidies and land rental fees, but exports are exempt from taxation. (7) Those engaged in agricultural product trading must obtain a license from the federal government, with a fee of 1,000 yuan, and those who delay obtaining a license will be fined. (8) When the basic agricultural products listed in this bill are imported from abroad, the import tax will be increased, and the increased tax rate will be equal to the tax levied on domestic trading of the same products. (9) After levying taxes on the buying and selling of agricultural products, in order to prevent agricultural product merchants from experiencing unexpected difficulties, they are allowed to borrow funds from the Finance Rehabilitation Corporation for assistance during the initial implementation period. (10) The basic agricultural products listed in this bill include cotton, wheat, cattle, pigs, rice, tobacco, sugar, and dairy products. Sugar was not initially included but was added at the last minute today. However, Philippine sugar was not included in the scope of this bill's relief. Therefore, it is stipulated that sugar imported from the Philippines after this will be subject to a compensatory tax (i.e., the increased import tax) according to the example of foreign products. However, the annual tax revenue, which is about 10 million yuan, will be allocated to the Philippine government. (11) Authorizing the President to suspend the implementation of this bill after the agricultural emergency is deemed to have been safely overcome. (National Telegram, 28th)

Ma Yinchu Observes the U.S. Abandonment of the Gold Standard 42

(Nanjing) Ma Yinchu's observations on the U.S. abandonment of the gold standard are as follows: The United States is the world's major gold-using country. The gold stored in the country accounts for more than 40% of the world's total. The unprecedented financial turmoil in the world recently occurred in this golden country. Although Roosevelt's handling was appropriate, the internal crisis was not fundamentally eliminated, and future changes are also unpredictable because the embers have not been extinguished, and there is a fear that the ashes will reignite.

Roosevelt's declaration banning gold exports is a temporary emergency measure, but knowledgeable people predict that Roosevelt will ultimately adopt a policy of abandoning the gold standard as a tool to adjust the U.S. economy. Without this, all relief bills will be difficult to achieve practical results. I believe that the reasons for the U.S. abandonment of the gold standard are, first, to raise prices to solve its domestic economic problems. The United States has overproduction, and due to the high tariffs of various countries and the changing standard, it is unable to sell its inventory. As a result, prices have fallen, rural areas have declined, factories have closed, society is unstable, and national tax revenue has decreased. Budget imbalances and other problems have followed one another. Therefore, the current solution must start with raising prices. After abandoning the gold standard, the policy of inflation can be used to raise prices, and the means of falling gold prices can be used to stimulate exports. Domestic industrial unemployment and financial issues can be solved accordingly. The Far East market has always been dominated by Britain, Japan, and the United States, but because Britain and Japan abandoned the gold standard one after another, the U.S. Far East market was severely hit. On the one hand, Japan used the means of falling yen prices to continue to develop the Far East market. On the other hand, it used trade income as military expenses for invading China, which was all detrimental to the United States. The United States had to use economic methods to suppress Japan's activities. Because after the devaluation of the U.S. dollar, U.S. goods could re-enter the Far East market. Once Japanese goods were unsalable, its domestic economic organization would undergo major changes. This kind of economic competition is enough to restrain the development of the Japanese. The purpose of Roosevelt's invitation to the British Prime Minister for talks was to seek the understanding of Britain and take joint action to deal with the ambitions of this East Asian aggressor. In addition, there is another reason, which is the policy of the Democratic Party. We know that the Democratic Party was originally based on the silver mine owners and agriculturalists in the southwestern provinces. The majority of the party hopes that the price of silver will rise and the price of raw materials will rise. Abandoning the gold standard is a shortcut to raising the price of silver and goods. At least part of Roosevelt's intention in doing this is to satisfy the wishes of his voters and consolidate his future political position. The reasons for the U.S. abandonment of the gold standard are roughly like this. The impact of this move on our country is that it can increase the people's purchasing power. When the U.S. dollar is expensive, goods priced at one U.S. dollar must be exchanged for four or five Chinese yuan. In the future, they may be able to be bought for two or three Chinese yuan. Also, U.S. books and machines are all needed by our country. After the devaluation, it is quite beneficial to China. Second, it can increase national tax revenue. After our country's purchasing power increases, foreign trade will gradually become active, and customs duties will also increase accordingly. However, the harm in this is also great. First, our country is an import-surplus country. The increase in imports is enough to hinder the development of the domestic industry, especially banks and industrial capitalists are the most disadvantaged. That is the first harm. Second, China's gold production has been almost exhausted in previous years. Now, because of the high price of silver, silver bars are continuing to flow out. The recent large-scale purchase of silver bars by foreign banks in Shanghai is clear proof of this. If this continues, it is inevitable that China's cash will run out. The government can issue strict orders to ban silver exports, but how to offset the repayment of foreign debts? Silver exports are likely to be banned by laws and regulations. As a result, China may be forced to become a paper currency standard. If the country changes to this point, the future is unbearable. (Special Dispatch, 29th)

U.S. Representative Davis Defends the British Disarmament Plan 82

Opposes German Rearmament

Washington Talks Show Results

Germany Still Insists on Equal Demands

The Future of Disarmament Faces Major Obstacles

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 28th - U.S. Representative Davis told the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference today that the United States will join other countries in refusing to overturn the British disarmament plan's amendments that are seeking to upset the balance of power. This statement by the U.S. representative is seen as the first result of the Washington talks and also as a sign that the United States has accepted the British plan, indicating that the Washington talks have gone further than official reports indicate. Davis's statement can also be seen as a warning to Germany, implying that the U.S. and Britain will not allow Germany to overturn the balance proposed by the British. The United States is determined to oppose Germany's rearmament.

At the same time, Germany also submitted an amendment today, suggesting expanding the elimination and destruction of defensive weaponry, expressing Germany's determination to demand equality. French Representative Massigli criticized the northern amendment, pointing out that it would destroy the British proposal. British Representative Eden also expressed surprise and said that he hoped that this amendment was not Germany's final word. The Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, Henderson, British Representative Eden, and German Representative Nadolny will hold a private meeting tomorrow to try to resolve various difficulties.

▲ National, Geneva, 28th - At today's meeting of the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference, German Representative Nadolny announced Germany's principles for disarmament. Nadolny stated that what Germany is asking for is nothing more than that the armament of each country, as stipulated in Article 8 of the League of Nations Covenant, should be reduced to the lowest limit consistent with common security and implemented. Furthermore, Germany should enjoy the same rights and guarantees as other countries in terms of territorial security, which has already been recognized by all countries. The British Foreign Minister once urged France to be patient and trust the future of the Disarmament Conference. Nadolny praised him, saying that only Germany has made every effort to understand the sincerity of opinions clearly, because Germany has been patiently waiting for 14 years for the completion of the disarmament plan promised by the great powers, but so far, no other country has taken concrete steps to reduce armaments. Can Germany still be considered to lack the concept of harmonious cooperation? Moreover, the principle of equality demanded by Germany should have been implemented immediately, but other countries have agreed to a transitional period. Article 8 of the League of Nations Covenant clearly states that disarmament should be completed immediately, but Germany has also agreed to the gradual implementation of disarmament. Therefore, Germany is now fighting for justice and equality again, which is the root of trust. Nadolny then explained the various reservations that Germany had put forward regarding the British proposal, one by one. The general idea of Germany's reservations is even more advanced than the British proposal, such as aggressive armaments, military aircraft, etc. Germany requires that they all be abolished and destroyed. Germany is also accepting a five-year transitional period, but after this, the equal status that Germany demands in the disarmament treaty should be established in fact. If other countries consider certain armaments to be indispensable for national defense, then the same armaments should not be withheld from Germany alone. After Nadolny announced Germany's disarmament objectives, German and French representatives exchanged views, but their attitudes were very firm. The French representative believed that if Germany insisted on this position, the result would be expansion of armaments rather than reduction of armaments. If Germany persists to the end, then the future Disarmament Conference will never be successful. Nadolny immediately declared again that Germany has no intention of rearming, but for the sake of territorial security, it must have the same guarantees as other countries. The German representative's declaration and the fierce debate after the declaration have made a very deep impression on the League of Nations. It is said that today, the time has come for countries to no longer avoid the points demanded by Germany and must find a solution. Judging from the individual declarations of the U.S. and Britain, they seem to be taking joint action and strongly disapprove of the verbal warfare between Germany and France.

▲ National, Geneva, 29th - The World Disarmament

Page 10

Conference has been open for fifteen months, and not only has it achieved nothing, but it is also about to encounter a new impasse. If Germany does not agree to compromise, there will be no possibility of breaking the deadlock. Furthermore, if the conference wants to establish an important document, then the definite attitude of the United States towards the consultation convention must also be clarified. According to reports, after the German representative put forward the demand last night that the disarmament convention must include a clause on Germany's complete equality of armaments in 1938, French Representative Massigli stated today that Germany's demands are difficult to accept. If this is Germany's last word, then there is no hope for any disarmament convention to be established. However, judging from the German representative's statement yesterday that paper equality can never satisfy the Germans, and Germany must have military equality and full rights to military equipment, its attitude is indeed very firm. As for the United States' attitude towards the consultation convention, there has been no official statement other than a telegram stating that the United States is willing to sign a consultation convention that does not bear substantial obligations, indicating that the United States will only agree to the principle of consultation and is unwilling to guarantee any future action. However, the first clause of the disarmament convention proposed by MacDonald requires that countries such as Britain, the United States, France, Germany, Italy, and Russia consult on joint action in accordance with the Non-Aggression Pact as a guarantee of security. The various obstacles that have arisen from the widespread unrest and suspicion in the world to agreeing to disarmament have not been slightly eliminated during Easter. The main ones are as follows: (1) France fears Hitler's Germany and the possible union of Germany and Austria, or the alliance of Germany, Italy, and Hungary, and therefore demands greater security as the price of disarmament; (2) Germany demands not only paper equality with France, but if France and its allies do not significantly disarm, Germany will rebuild its armaments; (3) The Little Entente fears the revision of treaties initiated by Germany and Italy; (4) Japan's militaristic behavior in the Far East makes countries with important interests in the Far East, such as Britain, the United States, and Russia, dare not greatly reduce their navies and air forces. Furthermore, China and Japan are of course not prepared to reduce their land, sea, and air forces; (5) The undeclared wars in South America also make representatives of South American countries hesitant to accept disarmament; (6) France and Italy have not joined the London Naval Treaty, making it impossible for Britain, the United States, and Japan to further reduce their navies; (7) Japan's statement that it wants to increase its naval ratio has further increased the sense of insecurity among countries. The above seven points are all major obstacles to the success of disarmament. As for the attitude of the United States, it is believed that although it will support genuine disarmament, it is unwilling to agree to join the actions of European countries to enforce the treaties they have concluded.

South American Bolivia-Paraguay Dispute 83

Bolivia Refuses Arbitration Solution

▲ Reuters, Buenos Aires, 28th - The Bolivian government today sent a long message to the governments of Argentina and Chile, rejecting the two countries' suggestion that the dispute between Bolivia and Paraguay should be resolved by arbitration, stating that this delaying solution would particularly benefit Paraguay. It also said that if Paraguay or Bolivia relied on the mediation of a third party to resolve purely private matters, it would be ridiculed as not knowing what it was doing by the two countries at war. Paraguay and Bolivia are fighting over a corner of the Gran Chaco. On July 30 of last year, the Chairman of the Council of the League of Nations intervened and sent a telegram to the two governments, asking them to pay attention to international obligations and saying that the two governments have now signed the League of Nations Covenant and must not use this as an excuse to start a war. Later, Paraguay agreed to cease hostilities, but demanded that Bolivia withdraw from the occupied territory. Bolivia also agreed to a truce, but on the condition that it be allowed to retain the original territory. In February of this year, hostilities resumed between the two countries, and the League of Nations took a firm stance, sending a telegram to the two governments, urging them to conclude a ceasefire agreement quickly.

Remains of British Aviator Discovered in Remote Italian Mountains 87

▲ Reuters, Florence, Italy, 28th: Law enforcement officials formally announced tonight that the wreckage of an aircraft discovered near Arezzo, along with a set of remains, has been confirmed to be those of British aviator Bert Hinkler. Hinkler departed from Feltham at 3:00 PM on January 7th, intending to set a new flight record between England and Australia. He subsequently disappeared without a trace. Today, Italian loggers discovered the wreckage of an aircraft in a remote area of the Apennine Mountains at an altitude of 4,600 feet. They immediately reported it to the police. According to information received by the British Embassy in Rome, the clothing on the deceased found in the plane was torn and tattered. He had a Canadian passport on his person, but the writing was blurred from exposure to the elements. Upon closer examination, it was identified as belonging to Hinkler. It is now believed that Hinkler died immediately upon impact, as the aircraft caught fire after the crash, and Hinkler's body was partially burned. The aircraft model was also identical to the one flown by Hinkler. It is therefore concluded that the deceased is undoubtedly Hinkler. Hinkler was the first person to fly solo across the South Atlantic Ocean from west to east. He was only forty years old. He was attempting to break the record of eight days, twenty hours, and forty-nine minutes for a flight between England and Australia, held by Scott, when he met this tragic end. It is indeed a loss for the British aviation community.

▲ Reuters, Florence, 28th: The site where Hinkler's aircraft crashed is five miles from the village of Monte Migliaio. Only a narrow path extending to the cliff face is passable, making it difficult to reach. The village only saw its first car two years ago. Hinkler's remains were found by a dog and had been partially eaten by wolves, resulting in dismembered limbs.

▲ Reuters, Florence, 29th: Hinkler's remains were wrapped in the Italian tricolor flag, with candles burning at his head and feet, and placed in the church of San Niccolò, guarded by huntsmen.

Many women are now entering the church to pray beside the body. It is said that the mountain where Hinkler met his fate is haunted by ghosts, and the villagers regard it with fear. Only those collecting charcoal occasionally venture up its slopes. It is now speculated that Hinkler must have been flying low at the time to search for a landing spot, but he inadvertently struck the mountainside, causing the crash. The aircraft was not severely damaged, but Hinkler was thrown out, his remains lying about seventy feet from the plane, buried in the snow until it melted and he was discovered. The Italian government will accord Hinkler's remains official honors.

Overview of the Fierce Battles at Gubeikou in Recent Days 88

From the 21st to the 26th

We Fight to the Death with Flesh and Blood Against Modern Weapons

The Center of the Battle is in the Nanti’anmen Area

Corpses Pile Up Like Small Hills in Front of Our Positions

Beijing Military News: Beginning at dawn on the 21st of this month, Japanese army infantry and artillery units, numbering approximately five to six thousand men, launched a fierce attack from the left flank of Gubeikou towards our Eight Towers and the North and South Xin'kai Ridge areas. At the same time, a large number of aircraft, together with heavy artillery, concentrated their bombardment on our Eight Towers high ground. Our defending soldiers fought to the death. The high ground was gained and lost several times. In the evening, both sides continued to engage in hand-to-hand combat under the cover of darkness. The Eight Towers was reduced to ashes due to the enemy's heavy bombing by numerous aircraft and artillery. At that time, our military casualties on the high ground amounted to over 1,200, including two battalion commanders killed and one seriously wounded. From 5:00 AM on the 22nd, the enemy launched another fierce attack, with part of their forces crossing the Chao River to attack our front. The enemy's artillery fire was exceptionally intense, and they fired over two hundred smoke bombs, using the smoke to launch their assault. Our troops also made use of the enemy's smoke to repeatedly counterattack, engaging the enemy in hand-to-hand combat up to five times. Corpses piled up like small hills in front of our positions. By 4:00 PM, the enemy, having repeatedly failed in their attacks, switched to concentrated artillery fire, continuously shelling key points of our positions. In the evening, they again used over a thousand infantrymen to attempt to outflank our left flank, North and South Xin'kai Ridge. Fortunately, our troops were prepared and immediately met them with a head-on assault, engaging in fierce fighting for several hours. The enemy was unable to withstand the attack and began to retreat towards the west side of Gubeikou. On this day, our military casualties included six company and platoon leaders killed and over six hundred soldiers killed or wounded. At 7:00 AM on the 23rd, seven enemy aircraft arrived over our positions and bombed them repeatedly. The enemy's heavy artillery again concentrated its fire, fiercely shelling our left flank positions at Nanti'anmen with over four hundred rounds. Later, at around 10:00 AM, they used smoke bombs to cover an infantry advance. Our troops waited for them to approach before opening fire with machine guns, followed by repeated hand-to-hand combat with hand grenades and bayonets four times. By 2:00 PM, our Eight Towers had been leveled by the enemy, and the company of infantry defending it perished together with the

On this day, our military casualties included seven company and platoon leaders killed or wounded, and over nine hundred soldiers killed or wounded. In the evening, the fighting subsided slightly, and the enemy's artillery fire also became less frequent. From 7:30 AM on the 24th, the enemy only used artillery fire to bombard us, and their infantry did not advance. At 2:00 PM, seven enemy aircraft arrived over our positions and dropped bombs. At the same time, their artillery fire gradually intensified, but the enemy only fired at our positions and dared not advance. Both sides remained locked in a stalemate until the evening. At night, the enemy's artillery still

Reasons for the Japanese Army's Withdrawal from Eastern Hebei 92

Japanese Army Transports Troops to Northern Manchuria to Deal with Soviet Russia

We Take Advantage of the Vacancy to Attack and Recapture Lost Territory in Eastern Hebei

Special Dispatch from Beijing: In recent days, tensions between Japan and Russia have escalated over the issue of Central Eastern Railway vehicles, with Russia and its puppet regime exchanging protests and engaging in heated written exchanges. The situation is becoming increasingly dire, with the possibility of Japan and Russia resorting to force. According to sources in Shenyang, although Soviet Russia has remained silent since the September 18th Incident, the situation has become critical as the Japanese side has instigated the establishment of a puppet state. The Russian authorities have repeatedly issued unofficial statements, indicating their willingness to risk their Five-Year Plan and engage in war. The Japanese side has also been secretly planning and preparing countermeasures. When the issue of vehicle seizures on the Central Eastern Railway arose, long-accumulated grievances could no longer be suppressed. In recent days, the Japanese army has redeployed a division from Japan, landing in Dalian and actively transporting them to northern Manchuria. A large amount of military supplies, such as aircraft, tanks, anti-aircraft guns, and ammunition, are also being transported with the troops. Japanese soldiers are also carrying items such as gas masks. The equipment they are carrying is mostly of the latest type. Their intentions are self-evident. At the same time, the Soviet Russian side has dispatched a large army of twelve divisions to Vladivostok, Khabarovsk, Chita, and the Amur region, and is also carrying out border immigration, transporting a large number of Russian civilians to garrison in the border areas as the front line of the Soviet Russian defense forces. More than 300 aircraft have been transported to Vladivostok and other places, which is particularly alarming to the Japanese side. As a result, the Japanese side had to hastily withdraw its troops from various places in eastern Hebei. Our troops were able to take advantage of the vacancy to attack and recapture the lost territories in eastern Hebei. Another theory is that the Japanese army's retreat is due to the upcoming Washington Conference. If they were to occupy Tianjin and Beijing at this time, it would infringe upon the interests of Britain and the United States in northern China, on the one hand causing a major international reaction, and on the other hand, the extension of the front line would make it difficult to balance economic and military strength. Therefore, they are thinking of taking the opportunity to change course and find other solutions. If this theory is credible, then the Japanese army's retreat this time has another purpose. (26th)

Nanchang Fortifies City Defenses 93

Conscripting Laborers to Construct City Defense Transportation Roads

Various Construction Costs Estimated at Approximately 120,000 Yuan

Nanchang Correspondence: All sectors of this city believe that amidst the crisis of the Red Bandits taking advantage of the Japanese army's advance on western Hebei, they have also launched a full-scale invasion from eastern Jiangxi. Nancheng, Yihuang, and Chongren have simultaneously issued urgent warnings. Linchuan and Dongxiang are also under considerable pressure. If Nanchang is not secured, the southeastern half of the province will be unimaginable. All sectors of the United Anti-Bandit Association convened a meeting on the 24th to discuss methods to consolidate provincial defenses and eliminate the Red Bandits. Attendees included representatives from various civic groups, commercial and academic circles, and local elders Hu Siyi (former Governor of Jiangxi Province), Peng Chengwan (former Military Governor of Jiangxi Province), and dozens of others. Xiong Shihui also attended and was present. Chairman Fan presided over the meeting and resolved to conscript laborers from this city to complete city defenses and send representatives to petition the Central Government, requesting Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to be stationed in Jiangxi Province to personally supervise the suppression of bandits. The original proposal is recorded below: (1) Chairman Xiong reported that he had inspected the city defense works of this city with Chairman He of Hunan Province yesterday and felt that they were not yet adequate. Nanchang is the provincial capital, and city defenses should be strengthened urgently. It is now planned to actively carry out the construction of moats, fortresses, transportation roads, and various city defense works to achieve a permanent solution. This will have a significant effect on military affairs, and a great benefit to the development of this city and transportation. It is now calculated that the most economical method will require more than 100,000 yuan for weapons, barbed wire, etc., about 200,000 yuan for dredging ditches, and about 100,000 yuan for fifty miles of transportation roads. Now that the government is determined to complete this important work, it is making every effort to save all expenses and cover them, but it is still short more than 100,000 yuan, and the situation is urgent. In order not to increase the burden on the people, and to achieve rapid results in practice, it is proposed to emulate the methods of other counties in conscripting labor to build roads, conscripting laborers from Nanchang City to build city defense transportation roads. This will not cost money and will demonstrate a sound spirit. However, regarding this conscription method, whether it is appropriate and feasible, everyone is urged to discuss it together with the intention of assisting in bandit suppression and concern for the local area. (Resolution) City defense transportation roads are necessary and should be built urgently. Committee members Li Shangyong and Peng Chengwan were elected to contact the highway department and the security bureau to jointly plan the conscription method. If conscripting labor is difficult, the association will assist in the construction, with the city defense construction cost being 120,000 yuan. (2) Committee members Huang Wenzhi and He Zhihuan proposed that other provinces generally consider the suppression of bandits in Jiangxi to be unimportant and regard it as a local problem. The association should make the whole country understand that the bandit disaster in Jiangxi is at stake for the survival of the entire Chinese nation, and request unanimous support to eliminate the Red Bandits as soon as possible in order to resist Japan with all our strength. Please make a resolution. (Resolution) A. Send representatives to the Central Government to request additional troops to Jiangxi to suppress the bandits. B. Telegraph the whole country, explaining the severity of the bandit disaster and its relationship to the survival of the entire nation, and separately telegraph Jiangxi native associations in various other provinces to petition the National Government to save the province. C. Petition Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to temporarily reside in Jiangxi to supervise the suppression of bandits until the Red Bandits are eliminated. (2) Chairman Tai proposed that all central government agencies stationed in the province should also follow the example of the two-tenths donation method for provincial civil servants from February to show assistance and set an example. (Resolution) Send separate letters to the central government agencies stationed in Jiangxi to follow the example. Other cases omitted. (April 25th)

He Long's Bandit Troops Clash 94

Bandit Army Chief of Staff Shen Zixiang Killed

Ammunition and Food Depleted, Internal Panic Occurs

Changsha Correspondence: The commander of the Communist Bandit's Third Army, He Long, has been disrupting the border areas of Hunan, Hubei, Shaanxi, and Sichuan for many years, without being eliminated. Last winter, after suffering losses in Hubei, he led his remnants to occupy the mountainous areas of the Shihhe, Longsang, and areas bordering Sichuan, Hubei, and Hunan. It has been several months. The Hubei army under Fan Xiji and the Hunan army under Chen Quzhen have been ordered to jointly suppress the bandits and are currently surrounding them. Yesterday, Chen Cexun, the magistrate of Sangzhi County and the captain of the security brigade, reported to He Jian about the internal clashes of He Long, as well as the depletion of ammunition and food among the bandit troops. The report is recorded as follows: (Respectfully submitted for the perusal of He Junjian, Chairman of the Changsha Provincial Government: (1) The Red Bandits Duan Dechang, Wang Bingnan, and the puppet Third Army Chief of Staff Shen Zixiang (from Zhejiang) were indeed killed by He Long in the Jinguoping area bordering Hefeng and Badong, labeled as being killed by the reorganization faction. (2) The puppet Third Army is now reorganized into the Seventy-ninth Division and a training regiment. The commander of the Seventy-ninth Division, Ye Guangji, and the political commissar, Shen Wen, are from Anxiang Township. The commander of the Ninety-ninth Division, Tang Fulin, is from Sangzhi. The political commissar, Song Panming, and the commander of the training regiment, Lu Dongsheng, are from Xiangtan. Each division has three regiments, each regiment has three companies, with no battalion system. Each company has 50-60 people, and the training regiment has about 700 people. The total number of combat troops is no more than 2,500 people. Except for the training regiment, each soldier has 5-6 clips of ammunition, and the rest have less than 10 rounds per gun. (3) The puppet Third Army political commissar Tao Xiangying (from Manchuria) was sent by Soviet Russia to work with the puppet Third Army's central sub-district chairman Xia Xi (from Yiyang) in the Third Army. Tao and Xia are in control of the puppet army. (4) Most of the puppet army soldiers are from the Hubei, Damen, and Qianjiang areas. The people are very panicked. (5) The bandit troops are short of ammunition and food, and they rely on looting local tyrants for daily living. They recently invaded the Wudaoshui area of Sangzhi because the bandits reported that Sangzhi had no garrison. After hearing that the garrison had not withdrawn, they immediately withdrew to Maoba, which belongs to Hefeng. I believe that the bandits have become fish in a kettle, and once Heaven sends an army, they can be eliminated immediately. This is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity that must not be missed. I humbly request that a brigade of troops be dispatched quickly at this time to thoroughly suppress them. This will achieve twice the result with half the effort, and we can rely on their elimination soon. This is respectfully submitted for your review. [Stamped] Sangzhi County Magistrate and Security Brigade Captain Chen Cexun) (April 27th)

Gu Zhutong Transferred to Henan

Shaanxi Disaster Increasingly Severe 96

Although it Rained Once, Wheat Seedlings Withered

Disaster Victims Unable to Farm, Continued Hope for Relief

Xi'an Correspondence: Since last winter, Shaanxi has not seen a drop of rain for several months, and the disaster situation is once again becoming severe. Up until the 23rd of last month, there was a welcome rainfall, and the wheat seedlings showed some hope of recovery. However, eight or nine out of ten had already withered and died. Furthermore, there were no seeds or farming tools to sow autumn crops, leaving the disaster victims lost and without a path to take. There was no way to escape, and no way to return. There were also those who heard rumors of relief and returned to their villages to seek survival, only to find that there was little porridge for many people. They waited for many days without

receiving anything, and some even starved to death as a result. This is particularly tragic and unbearable. Therefore, at this time of year when the old grain has run out and the new grain has not yet ripened, the disaster situation is becoming increasingly severe, and the hope for relief is greater than ever before. If no measures are taken to overcome this difficult situation,

the tragic situation will be even more unimaginable. The disaster conditions in various places after the rain are specially recorded in detail below. It is hoped that those who care about the Shaanxi disaster will pay attention to it.

Qian County 97

The county is located on a plateau, with no land that can be irrigated. Even when there is timely rainfall, households with little land often worry about not having enough. This time, after five years of drought, no crops were harvested. Even the formerly prosperous families have run out of food. The situation of the middle and lower classes can be imagined. Now, farming tools, clothing, trees, and houses have all been sold, leaving them with nothing to live on. Beggars fill the land and line the streets, and abandoned children cry everywhere, their voices exhausted, with no one willing to care for them. Selling daughters and wives has become a marketplace. Some die of hunger, others die in war. There are unburied corpses in the villages. Some migrate north to Gansu, others migrate south to Sichuan. There are few settled families along the villages. It is estimated that the population of Qian County is no less than 170,000 to 180,000. Those who remain are only six or seven out of ten, but they still do not cook during the day and guard against bandits at night. Their hardship and suffering are difficult to describe. As for the porridge kitchens providing relief, those who hold receipts to receive porridge are all emaciated and barely clothed. Those who do not have receipts number about several thousand. The strong stand on tiptoe, craning their necks, like hungry ghosts seeking food. The old and weak lie on the ground, heads bowed, like prisoners awaiting death. They guard the kitchens all day and wail all night, demanding an increase in porridge tickets and licking the spilled porridge on the ground outside the pots. The tragic situation cannot be described in detail.

Fufeng 98

Last year, in July, this county received urgent relief from the great philanthropist of Tianjin and the Shanghai Red Swastika Society. Many of those who received aid escaped to seek survival. The remaining elderly, weak, women, and children could not escape and could not survive. In the cold winter, they were about to starve to death. Later, philanthropists from Tianjin set up a porridge kitchen in Xinglin Town, issuing only 1,850 porridge tickets. Due to the small amount of porridge for many people, some who waited starved to death. It was too horrible to look upon. Who would have thought that this spring, disaster victims who had escaped to other places heard about the establishment of porridge kitchens and the distribution of relief, and more and more returned to their villages to seek relief. Although it has been raining in recent days, the villages have been reduced to rubble, and the vegetable roots have long been eaten. The summer harvest is already hopeless, and tens of thousands are waiting to be fed.

Xingping 99

Xingping is located on a plateau, and the disaster situation has been extremely severe in recent years. No eight grains have been harvested, and the farmers' economy has collapsed. Those who tear down houses and sell wives and children are too numerous to count. Although there has been welcome rainfall recently, the time for sowing autumn crops is not far off. However, extremely poor families still cannot get a single meal, and their lives are in danger. There are many such families.

Baoji 100

Baoji has experienced continuous drought for years, and no harvests have been gathered. Countless disaster victims in the entire county have died or been displaced. The elderly, weak, women, and children beg from door to door, a pathetic sight. Although there has been rain recently, there are no seeds, so there are many who cannot plant their land.

Fengxiang 101

Due to the prolonged drought in Fengxiang, the number of disaster victims fleeing is increasing daily. Those who have not fled have exhausted their food due to banditry. They are now digging and eating vegetable roots, and both hosts and guests are fighting over them, all falling into a sea of suffering. Therefore, they are also craning their necks and awaiting rescue.

Lintong 102

Wujiatun in Lintong has experienced continuous drought for years, and the summer and autumn harvests are uncertain. Coupled with disasters such as wind and insects and plagues, the situation is even more unspeakable. Of the existing population, only two or three out of ten remain. Although there has been welcome rainfall recently, the disaster victims still go hungry all day long, and those who starve to death by the roadside are seen everywhere. The situation is extremely tragic.

Chengcheng 103

Chengcheng is located in the remote foothills of northeastern Shaanxi Province. The land is barren and the people are poor. Even in good years, there is a risk of famine. After the seventeenth year of the Republic, it has suffered successive droughts. More than half of the people in the countryside have fled, leaving thousands of miles of red land and abandoned villages. Although there has been light rain from heaven recently, the tree bark and vegetable roots have already been dug up and eaten. The remaining disaster victims still have no way to make a living.

Heyang 104

In Heyang County, there were black frosts on the first, second, tenth, and eleventh of March, with the wheat and bean seedlings withering immediately. Grain prices soared. Although there was some rain during the vernal equinox, it was too little, too late. Recently, deaths and migrations have been heard of daily. And city and rural markets are full of people selling odd items, such as farming tools, furniture, old clothes, and toys. Few pay any attention. A cow or horse is worth only a few dollars. The severity of the disaster is too horrible to look upon.

Mei County 105

The disaster situation in the county is worsening daily. Everyone is out of food, and every household has run out of grain. The number of starving people who need relief to survive is at least 20,000. Deaths are increasing, and the situation has already evolved to the state it was in last year.

Qianyang 106

The territory of Qian County is full of mountains and ridges and has always been known to be barren and poor. There is a saying, "Qianyang and Longzhou, harvest nine out of ten years, and if one year is not harvested, you have to leave on your back." The thinness of its production can be imagined. Recently, the impact of drought and locusts has made the situation even more unbearable. Many have fled. An investigation of the county's population of more than 11,000 households revealed that before the rain, it was heard that more than half had fled, which is alarming. Although it has rained now, the wheat seedlings had mostly withered before the rain, and the harvest is still hopeless. Therefore, the lives of the general public are extremely difficult, reaching the extreme point. They are emaciated and the situation is extremely tragic.

Kunshan 107

Murder Case Occurs in the City

Sun Yaoshan, who runs a sugar mill on the south bank of the river, was having lunch at the Kunshan Restaurant at noon on the 28th with friends Chen Mubao and the monk Zhong Xiao. Sun, because Zhong was having an affair with his concubine, cursed at Zhong while drunk and then became violent. People persuaded them to stop and they dispersed. At 2:00 PM, the two met again in front of the Kunshan Theatre and repeated the fight. Zhong then took out a small axe he had hidden and slashed Sun in the neck, causing blood to flow like a fountain. Zhong, seeing the trouble he had caused, took the opportunity to escape. Sun was taken to the Guangren Hospital by friends for treatment. Doctor Gu used surgery to ligate the wound, but the main artery had been severed, and Sun died at 4:00 PM. Cheng Ruji, the director of the Public Security Bureau, upon hearing the news, immediately ordered the detective team to supervise and dispatch detectives to search for the perpetrator. He also dispatched police to take Chen Mubao and Wei Jinrong, Han Yun, and Long, who were at the scene trying to mediate, to the bureau to be interrogated in the county. He ordered personnel to examine the body in the morning and gave the detective team a deadline to capture the murderer and bring him to justice.

Center School Teacher Dies Suddenly

Qian Qifu, a teacher at the Pengban Town Central Primary School in the county, was usually healthy and loved sports. He lived on campus. The night before, colleagues heard him babbling in his sleep, but it soon stopped. On the morning of the 28th, his colleague Zhang was the first to arrive at school and called Qian to get up, but there was no response. He pulled back the curtain and saw that Qian's face was pale and he had been dead for some time. He immediately informed Principal Zhou, who reported it to the local public security substation and the Education Bureau. They are investigating the cause of Qian's death. Family members arrived at the school after hearing the news and transported the body back for burial. The cause of death is still unknown.

Songjiang 108

Songjiang Bank Debt Case Concludes

The Songjiang Bank creditor group representatives Bai Guanlan and others' lawsuit against Xie Liangda and others for debt has been going on for a long time. Although the liquidation office has disbursed funds, a verdict has not yet been reached. Yesterday was another hearing date. At 10:30 AM, Judge Wang Sixian opened the first court to continue the hearing. On the plaintiff side were the attorneys Bai Guanlan, Zhang Jiecai, and Qu Yue. On the defendant side was the attorney Sha Xunyi, representing Zhang Xiaomei and others. Both sides briefly debated. The plaintiff's attorney, following the court's instructions, petitioned to withdraw the cases of the 30 small creditors who had already received funds. Judge Yu then declared the debate closed and announced that a verdict would be announced on May 10.

Suzhou 109

Lake Bandits Discovered in Dongting West Mountain

Yesterday (the 29th), three bandit ships carrying over thirty bandits were discovered in the southern part of Dongting West Mountain, intending to rob West Mountain Town. After receiving a telegram from the local township office, the county government has dispatched a police team to pursue and suppress them.

Changzhou 110

Six-Year-Old Child Assassinated

Jinlong, the six-year-old son of You Qingxi, who lives on a bean boat on Dou Shi River outside the Fourth Gate of Wu Yi, suddenly left the boat at around 8 PM on the 27th and did not return after about an hour. His parents searched everywhere without success. Unexpectedly, at around 12 AM, Jinlong's body was found by the river near the ferry crossing. Upon retrieving the body, it was discovered that all the silver ornaments on his body had been taken. The Second Police Station of the Public Security Bureau reported the case and quickly identified Gu Wangshi and a monk named Chen as the main suspects. They were handed over to the County Court Procuratorate for interrogation. On the 28th, the supervising prosecutor led officials to conduct an autopsy, which confirmed that the child had been suffocated to death and then dumped into the river. After further interrogation at the court, the two suspects were ordered to be detained pending further investigation.

Wuxi 111

Boats Robbed on the Wuxi-Changzhou Route

A night boat, owned by boatman Zhu A’gen, has been operating between Wuxi and Changzhou, passing through the Mei Yan Bridge area, for some time. The boat was fully loaded with goods and passengers and departed from Xueqian the other day for Wuxi. However, when it reached Baishi Mountain in Wuxi, three bandits disguised as passengers pulled out handguns and ordered the boat to stop. The boatman had no choice but to order the crew to dock the boat. Unexpectedly, four or five more bandits jumped onto the boat from the shore and began a large-scale search and robbery. Passengers were robbed of over one hundred silver dollars, and goods worth a total of 326.50 yuan were stolen. After plundering, the bandits boarded a small boat on the opposite bank and rowed away. Boatman Zhu A’gen, seeing that the bandits were far away, quickly sent a crew member ashore to report to the Xue Yan Bridge Security Corps. Upon receiving the report, Wu Zongjie, the head of the Corps, immediately dispatched militiamen to guard the Li Jiang Kou. Upon receiving the news, the Hu Dai Commercial Corps also dispatched a team to encircle and pursue the bandits from both Bai Shi Mountain and Qing Ming Bridge, but without success.

Investigation and Arrest of Villagers for Selling Poison Pills Causes Uproar

The local Narcotics Investigation Office dispatched two inspectors, accompanied by armed patrol officers, by boat to Yang Fushun's residence in Tianshangshi, District Five, where they discovered a large number of opium quitting pills. Yang was taken aboard the boat. Subsequently, they raided a red pill den in Tangtou Town, District Six, and also took the owner of the den, Zhang, and his partner, A, aboard the boat. Unexpectedly, when they arrived near Miaoshutou, over 300 villagers suddenly appeared, claiming that the investigators were harassing the people and demanding that the investigators and the boat be detained. During the commotion, the red pills and the three arrested individuals, including Yang, were released by the villagers. Later, the inspectors reported the incident to Director Chen in the city, who forwarded the report to Director Shen of the Jiangsu Provincial Narcotics Investigation Office, who ordered a strict investigation and arrests. Director Chen, upon receiving the order, immediately dispatched Team Leader Gong Guilin and Inspector Shen Dehua, leading police officers to the countryside to investigate and make arrests. However, before Team Leader Gong and his men arrived at Miaoshutou, the villagers had already heard the news and gathered hundreds of people again, preparing to cause an uproar. The officers arrested six individuals who had caused trouble: Guo Yuexuan, Guo Xingbao, Guo Ziqin, Liu Honggen, Guo Daoshi, and the village head, Guo Jinchen, and took them to the investigation office for processing. After questioning them, Director Chen ordered the release of village head Guo Jinchen on bail, as he was deemed to be uninvolved, while the other five were detained pending further review.

Qingjiang 112

Currency Trade Abolishes Taels and Converts to Yuan

The local currency exchange shops have been discussing the abolition of taels and the conversion to yuan for some time. The following six measures have been finalized: (A) All silver deposits, loans, and transactions will be settled in silver dollars at an agreed price of 6.8625 mace by the end of April; (B) Starting from May 1st, trading in Zhen exchange, town exchange, and copper yuan will commence, with price fluctuations determined by market supply and demand; (C) Zhen exchange will be delayed by four days, and Shen exchange will be delayed by five days. Businesses and merchants who settle payments in Shenzhen will follow the respective delay periods. If settling in Zhen foreign currency, delay by five days; if settling in Shen foreign currency, delay by seven days; (D) Starting from May 1st, all transactions will be denominated in foreign currency; (E) Merchants who entrust remittances to Shenzhen will be charged 7.5 li per 100 yuan above the market rate, plus a handling fee of 5 fen. Foreign currency deposits are not counted; (F) Shops that entrust remittances to Shenzhen will be charged 1 jiao per 100 yuan above the market rate, with an additional handling fee of 1 jiao.

Huzhou 113

Erdu Town Plundered by Bandits

Erdu Town, located about fifteen li from the county seat of Wukang, has over twenty stores. It is a prosperous commercial center, especially now that tea and bamboo shoots are being marketed. Unexpectedly, at around 5 PM on the 26th, over twenty bandits speaking with a Henan accent, armed with guns, stormed into the town. They first surrounded the Public Security Substation and disarmed the police officers. Police officer Chen Fulai was shot and killed by the bandits, and two other officers were also wounded. The bandits confiscated four Mauser rifles. After obtaining the rifles, the bandits split up and ransacked various stores throughout the town, including Wang Tonghe’s general merchandise store, Zhengchang General Merchandise store, Xiechang Sauce Garden, a tea and bamboo shoot shop, and a pharmacy, resulting in a total loss of over 3,000 yuan.

Pinghu 114

All Sock Factories Suspend Operations

The local sock factories have recently been facing difficulties due to the inspection of purchased yarn and tight credit, making it impossible to continue operating. Therefore, a meeting of the trade association was convened at 1 PM yesterday. Representatives from 24 factories attended, including Guanghua, Huatong, Tongyi, Yuhua, Yixin, Shunfeng, Zhenfeng, Minghua, Minsheng, Minqiang, Zhenhe, Rixin Chang, Qinxin, Rongji, Hengjiu, Zhenxing, Dingcheng, Yucheng, Tongyuan, Jiuhe, Dahua, Xiexing, Qin Yu, and Lunxin. It was decided to suspend all machinery operations and sell off existing stock. If the factories still have yarn in stock, they must finish it within a very short period and refrain from purchasing more yarn to show their determination.

Ningbo 115

Security Corps Squad Leader Commits Suicide

Lu Risheng, the squad leader of the Qian’an Hu Township Security Corps in the second district of Zhenhai, was usually diligent in his duties. Unexpectedly, he became mentally deranged due to some recent stimulation, leading to abnormal behavior. At 8 AM yesterday, he used a wooden roof tile to strike himself in the headquarters, hitting a vital point and dying instantly. After inspection by county officials, it was confirmed that he had committed suicide. The township office prepared a coffin for burial and notified his family to claim the body.

Temporary Martial Law for Tomorrow's Labor Day 116

Measures Determined for Prevention in May

The police authorities of the Chinese-administered areas of the city have decided to increase security measures from May 1st to the 31st. Tomorrow, being May 1st, Labor Day, the security will be especially tight.

Security in Chinese-Administered Areas 117

The Supervisory Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the police stations in each district have been ordered to strengthen security starting from May 1st. All commemorative days will have double posts on major roads, and all police personnel will be deployed. The police brigade and the patrol car team will also be deployed for patrol, checking suspicious pedestrians and prohibiting associations, gatherings, and parades. All teams of the Municipal Security Office will also be fully deployed. The patrol team of the Garrison Headquarters will be dispatched for patrols.
