All police stations in the French Concession have also been ordered to increase security.

May 1st Security 118

Tomorrow is May 1st, Labor Day, the first commemorative day of May. The authorities in the Chinese-administered areas are deeply concerned that reactionary elements will incite workers under the guise of commemorating Labor Day and take action. It has been decided to implement strict security measures starting from 1 AM, and if necessary, temporarily close the iron gates at the boundaries of the Chinese-administered areas, only opening small pedestrian gates to facilitate traffic and provide a means of prevention. The General Labor Union has scheduled a "May 1st" commemorative meeting at the Municipal Party Headquarters at 9 AM.

Ministry of Finance to Rectify the Farmland Tax Surtax Law 119

Four Key Points to be Implemented Soon

Since the administration of farmland tax was delegated to local authorities, provinces have not made significant changes to the regular tax, but have arbitrarily increased surtaxes levied along with the regular tax, increasing the burden on the people. The Ministry of Finance, recognizing this, has long followed the teachings of the Premier Sun Yat-sen and formulated measures to limit surcharges, issuing repeated orders for compliance. However, local governments often use additional farmland tax as a source of revenue when implementing new policies, increasing the surtax day by day, to the point where it is several times the regular tax, with no end in sight. They even create ingenious names and issue separate receipts to avoid responsibility for violating the law. The people have repeatedly appealed to the central government, and although the Ministry of Finance has corrected this from time to time, the provinces have not fully complied. At the Second National Internal Affairs Conference of this session, the Ministry of Finance made a special proposal on this matter, and has recently drafted several articles of a draft law to rectify the farmland tax surtax based on the proposal, which has been passed by a meeting of relevant ministries and commissions and is expected to be implemented soon. Its key points can be divided into four categories: (1) The combined regular tax and surtax must not exceed 1% of the land value. In counties where land value has not been assessed, the surcharge should not exceed the regular tax for the time being. (2) All mu taxes and items levied with the tax shall be considered surcharges. (3) A deadline for rectification is specified, requiring completion by the deadline. (4) When necessary, the Ministry of Finance may send personnel to jointly rectify with the local government to gradually bring local finances into order.

Victory Report from Weng Zhaoyuan's Troops 120

Recapture of Funing and Fierce Battle at Yanhezhuang

A certain organization in this city received a telegram from the front lines stating that the right wing of Weng Zhaoyuan's troops launched a fierce attack on the enemy at Funing at the time of Wei (1-3 PM) on the 27th. The enemy initially resisted stubbornly but eventually collapsed and fled eastward. Our troops occupied Funing County at the time of You (5-7 PM) on the 27th and are still in pursuit.

In other news, the left wing of Weng's troops engaged in a fierce street battle with over 400 enemy troops at Yanhezhuang on the afternoon of the 26th, killing six enemy captains and dozens of soldiers, capturing over ten horses and three Japanese puppet flags.

French Female Aviator Departs Shanghai 121

French female aviator Ms. Hélène Boucher arrived in Shanghai from Beiping the other day and departed Shanghai for Hong Kong at 7 AM yesterday in her 300-horsepower aircraft, heading to Vietnam and India on her way back to France. French Consul-General Meyrier and many French and foreign residents went to the Hongqiao airfield to see her off. Ms. Boucher stayed at the French Consul-General's residence the other day after arriving in Shanghai. Although the clouds were heavy and low yesterday morning, which was unfavorable for aviation, Ms. Boucher resolutely drove to the airfield, inspected the engine, boarded the aircraft, bid farewell to the people of Shanghai, and took off into the sky.

Proceedings of the International Health Conference 122

Talk by Wu Liande

Research on Yellow Fever is Prohibited

Specialized Schools to be Established for Malaria

The Eastern Affairs Advisory Committee of the Health Organization of the International League of Nations held a general meeting of its members in Singapore at the end of last month to discuss health issues in Eastern countries. China sent Mr. Wu Liande, Director of the Harbor Quarantine Office, to attend the meeting as a representative. Mr. Wu has completed his mission and returned to Shanghai on the 22nd of this month. The reporter of the Dabaisha newspaper made a special visit to Mr. Wu at the Harbor Quarantine Office yesterday morning and asked him for details on the proceedings of the meeting. Mr. Wu informed us as follows:

No Research on Yellow Fever 123

According to Mr. Wu, the Eastern Health Advisory Committee of the International League of Nations is composed of representatives from Eastern countries and specializes in discussing Eastern health issues. A general meeting is held every two years. This session was held in Singapore last month. China sent me as a representative to attend the meeting, which began in Singapore on the 21st of last month. Thirteen countries participated in the meeting, which lasted four days. The most important issues discussed were three: The first point was yellow fever. This disease is virulent, and once it infects a human body, it is difficult to treat. It spreads very quickly, leading to death. It originates in places such as Africa and South America, and it is not easily transmitted to distant places. However, due to the convenience of transportation, there is a danger of it spreading widely. Therefore, the general meeting decided that places where this disease has not yet occurred should not research this disease. If this bacterium is researched, the bacterium may be sucked up by mosquitoes and fly to various places with airplanes, and it can be widely spread at any time, which is extremely dangerous.

Schools for Malaria 124

Malaria is a common disease in various countries at present. However, this disease is difficult to treat once infected, and it is especially difficult to eradicate. Various countries feel that it is necessary to conduct in-depth research on this disease. Therefore, it was decided to establish a malaria school in Singapore, and countries will select medical students who have already graduated from medical schools and experienced doctors to attend the school to specialize in researching various perfect methods for preventing and treating malaria. The research period is tentatively set for one year, after which they will return to their countries to implement the methods to rapidly eliminate malaria.

Praise for Our Treatment of Cholera 125

Cholera is one of the most prevalent, rapidly spreading, and dangerous diseases in various countries. The speed of death is truly shocking. Treatment methods are often delayed, making it impossible to save patients. More than 20% of those suffering from cholera in various countries die. In our country, because we administer preventive injections before cholera occurs and administer saline injections for emergency treatment when it occurs, we prioritize speed. Therefore, the death rate is only 7%. Various countries are very surprised by this. After I explained our country's treatment methods, various countries greatly praised it.

Issue of Inspection Rights for Factories in the Concession Shanghai Consular Body Has Requested Instructions from Their Home Countries 128

No Reply Yet to Shanghai Municipal Government's Protest

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement intends to obtain the right to inspect our country's factories by amending the Annex to the Yangjingbang Regulations. Consular Body Requests Instructions 129

After receiving Mayor Wu's formal letter of protest, the consuls stationed in Shanghai, in addition to exchanging informal opinions among themselves, immediately telegraphed the key points of Mayor Wu's protest to the ambassadors of their respective countries in China and the diplomatic authorities in their respective home countries, awaiting a reply before scheduling a discussion on a response. Our Side's Attitude 130

Since receiving Mayor Wu's report, the central authorities have generally agreed that the Council's move is related to the national administrative sovereignty, and the government cannot relax a single step. Defecting Communist Luo Zhanglong 136

Publishes Declaration Stating Past Mistakes

Central News Agency: Luo Zhanglong, also known as Luo Aojie, the Communist who recently defected in Shanghai, was originally scheduled to report on his defection at the Municipal Government Information Office yesterday morning. However, because he went to Beijing the other day and was unable to return in time, Ma Shaowu, a special investigator stationed in Shanghai by the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, gave the statement on his behalf. Luo himself also published a declaration of defection. Excerpts are recorded below:

Ma Shaowu: Statement on Behalf of Luo 137

Luo Zhanglong, formerly known as Aojie, is 32 years old and from Dongxiang, Liuyang County, Hunan Province. He graduated from the Department of Philosophy at Peking University. In 1923 (the 12th year of the Republic of China), he joined the Communist Party during the Kuomintang-Communist cooperation. Later, he was expelled by the Cadre Faction for opposing the Communist Party's violent policy. Luo then established his own faction and organized the Extraordinary Committee, which was not related to Chen Duxiu's Trotskyist faction. Luo has been working secretly in Shanghai for several years. He was arrested by the Municipal Public Security Bureau at the Commercial Library of Tianhougong Bridge, and after explaining the mistakes of the Chinese Communist Party to him, Luo defected. With Sun Zhengyi and Peng Yujie as guarantors, he was escorted to Beijing by personnel sent by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. He is currently temporarily residing at the Central Party Department Reception Center and has regained his freedom. Mr. Cai Yuanpei had previously requested bail from the Central Government in the name of the Civil Rights Protection League, but he did not know that Luo had already obtained his freedom. Luo himself also issued a declaration, expressing his past mistakes and future efforts. Luo has studied politics and economics and has published many works. It is hoped that he can work for the Party and the country in the future, which will also be welcomed by us.

Luo Zhanglong: Declaration of Surrender 138

The Chinese Revolution is now encountering a severe historical crisis. Since the September 18th Incident the year before last, the life-and-death issue of the entire nation has been placed before every citizen. Recently, the brutal aggression of Japanese imperialism in the North has further spurred unanimous indignation throughout the country. Considering the current situation, saving the precarious fate of the Chinese nation hinges on the sincere unity of the entire nation and a planned resistance against imperialism. The Chinese National Revolution must also be thoroughly completed through this. This is an indisputable principle. However, precisely during the development of the war of resistance against Japan, the policies of the Chinese Communist Party (CCP) are in direct opposition to this, causing significant constraints on the government. Based on this major, real event, and after a long period of deep consideration, I firmly believe that the Third International, which currently leads the CCP, is absolutely incapable of undertaking the task of the Chinese Revolution and, on the contrary, has become an obstacle to it. The completion of the Chinese Revolution can only be realized by relying on the guidance of the Three Principles of the People and the leadership of the Chinese Nationalist Party (KMT). Therefore, I now resolutely declare my departure from the CCP, abandoning my previous political prejudices, acknowledging all the mistakes I have made in the past, and bravely transitioning to the banner of the Three Principles of the People, becoming a combatant against communism and resisting Japan to complete the National Revolution. Now, I will briefly narrate my transition process as follows. In the early stages of the introduction of socialism into China, I began to study socialism. Subsequently, through the introduction of Li Dazhao, I joined the CCP in Beijing. I successively participated in activities among students and workers. Over the years, I held positions in branches, district committees, provincial committees, and central departments. At that time, with pure faith and ardent expectations for the world revolution, I worked diligently for communism, often standing on the front lines of struggles. When the issue of KMT-CCP cooperation arose, intense disputes occurred within the CCP. At this time, I once participated in KMT work. I experienced great wavering regarding the theory of "Communist Revolution versus National Revolution." After the failure of the CCP in 1927, it adopted an anarchist policy of violent uprisings, treating murder and arson as child's play, committing heinous crimes. At that time, I immediately believed that the CCP's path (which was actually the path of the Third International) had completely departed from China's actual needs and ran counter to the interests of the people. As a result of severely criticizing this absurd policy, I was subjected to various slanders by the CCP Central Committee. At the CCP's Sixth National Congress, the CCP's policy of violent uprisings was revived in the form of a false "Three Lines." I also suffered their attacks for continuing to resist. In 1930, when the CCP held the Fourth Plenary Session, I, along with Xu Xigen, Wang Kequan, Sun Zhengyi, and others, rose up in opposition and organized the Extraordinary Committee. Due to the failure of our resistance, we were

expelled from the CCP. Since then, my attitude towards politics has

become one of disappointment and passivity. However, I still retained a glimmer of hope, hoping that the CCP could discover a more correct path and solve the problem of the Chinese Revolution. Subsequently, this hope gradually disappeared. When the Extraordinary Committee was disbanded, and later when I attempted to restore it, I was extremely pessimistic and distressed in politics, and my political life came to a standstill. However, this led me to begin thinking about various fundamental issues of the revolution. Looking at it now, over the years, in politics and organization, I have seen through that the actions of the Third International and the CCP it leads are completely unsuited to the Chinese Revolution. I have understood that China is currently facing both foreign aggression and internal troubles, and the people are suffering immensely. The CCP bears a major responsibility. At this time, I was unable to fundamentally break with it and still wanted to seek remedies under the influence of its errors. This was not only a personal subjective error but also ignorance of objective truth. I now bravely acknowledge this error and am willing to reveal its most important points. First, China is a semi-colonial country. China's economy has long been under the control of international capitalism, and a strong national capital has not been formed. Fundamentally, the conditions for communist collective production do not exist. Therefore, the nature of the Chinese Revolution is primarily to eliminate feudal remnants internally and expel the forces of imperialism in China externally, so as to develop the economy and stabilize people's livelihoods. At the same time, the driving force of the Chinese Revolution should be the united strength of all classes, striving together to eliminate powerful enemies and complete the task. However, the CCP, based on the erroneous estimation of the Third International, disregarded all objective facts and arbitrarily issued a call to establish Soviet power, denying the existence of revolutionary forces other than the proletariat. This kind of transplantation of foreign, unrealistic theories resulted in the establishment of so-called Soviet power only causing widespread massacres, deaths, famines, and bankruptcies in rural areas. The launching of strikes, disputes, and armed uprisings in urban areas plunged the toiling masses into the same tragic fate. This fundamental error naturally created the main source of all other evils and formed the main reactionary current in the country. Second, the policies of the CCP all stem directly from the Third International. However, based on past observations, the errors of the Third International regarding the Chinese problem have been mentioned above. Moreover, its tactical inconsistency and constant contradictions are too numerous to count. The CCP's several performances of "opportunism" all

had the factions of the Third International as their backdrop. Furthermore, it always shifted the blame to individual members of the CCP, fueling internal strife within the CCP to facilitate its manipulation. At the same time, since 1918, after the Third International's hope for assistance from the Western European proletarian revolution was disappointed, all its foreign policies shifted to centering on supporting the Soviet Union. Consequently, it colluded with France and Japan and advanced its troops into the Middle East Railway. Its so-called assistance to weak and small nations and the carrying out of world revolution became nothing more than a pleasant-sounding term. Under the guidance and deception of the Third International, the Chinese Revolution was simply reduced to a sacrifice for supporting the Soviet Union. Third, the CCP's ignorant theories and its inherited selfish and arrogant policies of the Third International, repeatedly proven by the facts of more than a decade, are definitive proof that it will never become a "proletarian party." Therefore, the CCP is often like a structure built on sand; its foundation is completely empty and fluid. It not only lacks the support of the majority of the people but also cannot be said to be the vanguard of the revolution. On the contrary, genuine revolutionaries are now increasingly hostile to and leaving it. Only a few party officials are still falsely setting up organizations, hoping to build some kind of foundation on this ruin. This is nothing more than deceiving themselves and will ultimately lead to destruction. Fourth, the CCP's arrogant theories and distorted organization, needless to say, are bound to be buried in the development of the correct revolutionary path. However, even today, it is still actively exerting its counter-revolutionary efforts. Amidst the nationwide economic panic and the difficulties that surround it, what they are doing most vigorously is dashing east and west within the bandit-controlled areas, restraining the government's anti-Japanese forces to serve their narrow selfish goals. They are causing disturbances in all rural areas, taking advantage of the chaos to loot and plunder. In the production sector, they are creating disturbances, hindering production, and increasing unemployment. All of this can be interpreted today as pro-foreign behavior that is hostile to the national anti-imperialist front. However, they use various excuses to slander the ruling KMT for all this pro-foreign behavior. Based on the above points, I firmly believe that the First International and the CCP are, objectively speaking, reactionary groups in the history of the Chinese Revolution. A strict critique of my past participation in this group's words and actions naturally reveals my sins. I also deeply regret that in recent years, many young people have lost their political direction and suffered the same fate under the leadership of the CCP, which is full of errors, and have made huge sacrifices. Thus, after lengthy consideration and the KMT authorities' earnest explanations, I am today completely extricated from the mire of the CCP.

I correctly understand that the Three Principles of the People has a political program of action that is in line with the current political reality of China, as well as lofty and great goals and ideals. The ruling KMT has a glorious history in the Chinese Revolution and is currently supported by the broad masses. The urgent political issues in China today are to resolutely resist Japan and suppress communism under the leadership of the KMT government, to open up a new path for the nation, to reconcile class contradictions, to replace riots and terror, to implement a planned economy, to improve rural life, and to establish a new country that is of the people, by the people, and for the people. Luo Zhanglong, April 28th.

Anti-Drug Association Welcomes Zheng Yanfen 140

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, in light of Mr. Zheng Yanfen, Secretary of the League of Nations, recently returning to China from Geneva to investigate the domestic opium situation, held a welcome reception at the Deng Tuomo Hotel on Sichuan Road at 4 p.m. the day before yesterday. Those in attendance included committee members of the association: Wang Jingqi, Li Denghui, Shen Junru, Ding Shujing, Yin Zhufu, Chu Huiseng (acting), Huang Jia-Hui, etc. Chairman Wang Jingqi began by giving a welcoming speech. Then, Mr. Zheng Yanfen stood up and reported on the League of Nations' handling of anti-smoking affairs. He first explained the increase in members of the League of Nations' Advisory Committee on Narcotics and the staff of the League of Nations Secretariat's Opium Problems Department since 1930, as well as its impact on international anti-drug work. He then analyzed the nature and main points of the 1931 Convention for Limiting the Manufacture of Narcotic Drugs, and pointed out, from legal and practical aspects, that the Convention was more progressive than the previous two Opium Conventions of 1912 and 1925. He then described the situation of the Bangkok Conference on Prohibiting Smoking the year before last, and the League of Nations' work on opium smoking and cultivation, and the problems that still need to be solved in practice. Finally, he expressed the hope that the Anti-Drug Association would continue its efforts and effectively liaise with international anti-smoking organizations in order

to achieve the goal of anti-drug. After the report, Chairman Wang Jingqi gave a thank-you speech. Then, Huang Jia-Hui, the association's director-general, reported on the association's affairs and the domestic opium situation. Yang Renlao, director-general of the Fujian Anti-Drug Branch, reported on the opium situation in Fujian, stating that after the administration of the 19th Route Army, no effort was spared in prohibiting smoking. The provincial government issued a detailed circular, strictly prohibiting the planting of opium seedlings in all districts of the province during the autumn of this year. All fields must be planted with grains, and violators will be severely punished. It is expected that the opium seedlings in Fujian Province will disappear this year. It was already 7:30 p.m., and the guests and hosts parted on good terms. It is reported that after this long discussion with the committee members of the Anti-Drug Association, Mr. Zheng had a very clear understanding of the domestic opium situation, and his impression of the association was also very deep. He will soon depart for Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Singapore to conduct a detailed investigation of the opium situation. When he returns to Europe, he also plans to vigorously promote the situation of the Anti-Drug Association internationally. It is heard that anti-drug organizations in Fuzhou, Xiamen, Singapore, and other places are actively preparing to welcome Mr. Zheng.

Chief of Reception and Dispatch of the Sanshui Line Telegraph Company Took Oath Yesterday Morning 144

The Ministry Dispatched Wen Yuqing, etc., to Take Over on May 1st

After the rights to receive and dispatch telegrams for the Great Northern, Great Eastern, Pacific, and Sanshui Telegraph Companies were taken back, the three chiefs of reception and dispatch, Pan Cheng..., Sun Xichen, Li Jiqing, and all 14 assistants, took their oaths of office at the International Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications on Hede Road yesterday morning at 10 a.m. Wen Yuqing, the Director of the Bureau, presided over the ceremony, and Guo Shirong, Section Chief of the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, was the oath supervisor. The details of the inauguration are recorded below.

Attending Guests 145

The guests attending included Rong Baocheng, Director of the Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, Shen Fuhai, Chief Engineer of the Sanshui Line, He Jiacheng of the Telegraph Personnel Welfare Association, Wang Dabing, General Manager Chen of the Shanghai-Hankou Line, Tang Yong, representative of the International Radio Station Engineer, and more than 20 other people.

Order of the Meeting 146

(1) Opening of the meeting; (2) All stand at attention; (3) Pay the highest respect to the national flag and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; (4) The chairman respectfully reads Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will; (5) Silent tribute; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Chiefs of reception and dispatch of various Sanshui Line companies take their oaths: 1. Chief takes oath; 2. Deputy Chief takes oath; 3. Assistants take oath; (8) Supervisor's admonition; (9) Chief's representative's reply; (10) Taking photos; (11) Closing of the meeting.

Inauguration Personnel 147

The personnel who took the oath of office are as follows: (1) Great Northern: Chief Cheng Jiong, Deputy Chief Aier Side, Assistants Han Zuling, Pan Yongyi, Shen Qianli, Sheng Zhicheng; (2) Great Eastern: Chief Sun Xichen, Deputy Chief Shi Tao Lai, Assistants Zhang Gaodi, Yuan Lin, Hu Jiazhen, Sun Liangcai; (3) Pacific: Chief Li Jiqing, Deputy Chief Heimusi, Assistants Sun De, Li Wan, Wu Xuecheng, Zhao Ronghuan; (4) Beijing Road Reception and Dispatch Branch: Assistants Sun Yizhi, Chen Shaosheng.

Oath of Office 148

At 10 a.m., the bell rang to open the meeting. The ceremony was conducted according to protocol. Wen Yuqing, Director of the International Telegraph Bureau, gave a speech. The chiefs, deputy chiefs, and assistants of the three Sanshui Line companies took their oaths, saying, "I solemnly swear that I will strictly abide by Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will, obey the party's doctrines, abide by laws and regulations, and be loyal and diligent in my duties. I will never waste a single line or misuse a single person, and I will never engage in embezzlement or accept bribes. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment. This I swear." Guo Shirong, Section Chief of the Third Section of the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, the oath supervisor, gave an admonitory speech. Li Jiqing, the chief representative, and Shi Tao Lai, the deputy chief representative, replied successively. The ceremony ended at 11 a.m., photos were taken, and the meeting was adjourned.

Chairman's Speech 149

Wen Yuqing, Director of the International Telegraph Bureau, said in his speech: "Ladies and gentlemen, today is the oath-taking ceremony for the chiefs, deputy chiefs, and assistants of the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific Sanshui Companies appointed by the Ministry of Communications. We all understand that the three companies have a long history in China and are very well-managed. Their past achievements in serving society are worth commemorating. However, in the past, all matters relating to receiving and dispatching telegrams were handled entirely by their respective companies. Regarding this point, I want to solemnly say that it is in conflict with our National Government's Outline of National Reconstruction, because the Outline of National Reconstruction states that all telecommunications and transportation undertakings should be managed by the state. Not only is it inconvenient for foreigners to overstep their authority, but Chinese people are also not allowed to operate them privately. This is a matter of the sovereignty of the entire country. That is why I want to emphasize this point in particular, and I hope that all of you chiefs, deputy chiefs, and all sectors, Chinese and foreign, will have a deeper understanding of this point. When the contracts of the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific Sanshui Companies expired at the end of 1930, the National Government, based on the principles of the Outline of National Reconstruction, decided to take back and manage the undertaking itself. After many discussions, it was recently agreed that the rights to receive and dispatch telegrams for each company should be returned to us first. As for all the past circumstances, you are all very clear, so I will not talk about them anymore. Now, we have decided to officially take over the rights to receive and dispatch telegrams for the three companies the day after tomorrow (May 1). Why do the chiefs, etc., have to have this oath-taking ceremony before taking office? My personal feeling is that it has two meanings: (1) Because the past achievements of each company have been very good, we must manage them even better after taking over, so as not to fail the government's trust and the expectations of all sectors; (2) The telecommunications business is a business that serves the public. We should embrace the spirit of serving human communication and seek happiness for society, and we must not be induced by money or coerced by power and lose our inherent vocation. These two points are my personal feelings about this oath-taking, and I offer them as a guide to all oath-takers."

Supervisory Admonition 150

Guo Shirong, Section Chief of the Third Section of the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, the oath supervisor, said in his admonition: "The Sanshui Telegraph Company has always been a matter of common concern to China and foreign countries, and it is extremely important for international communication and the evolution of civilization. After the recovery this time, I hope that my colleagues will be sure to fulfill their responsibilities, strive to improve, and strive to develop and promote it."

Chief's Reply 151

Li Jiqing, Chief of Reception and Dispatch of the Pacific Sanshui Line, and Shi Tao Lai, Deputy Chief of Reception and Dispatch of the Great Eastern, gave replies successively. Li said, "Chinese international telecommunications has always relied on the reception and transmission of the Sanshui Telegraph Company. However, the right to receive and dispatch has always belonged to the three companies, and it cannot be denied that this hinders our national sovereignty. Therefore, in 1930, the Ministry of Communications, in view of this, decided to negotiate with the companies to recover it in order to respect sovereignty. Later, after dispatching personnel to contact them, the companies also believed that this should be the case, so the negotiations went very smoothly. Now it has been officially recovered. From now on, with Sino-foreign cooperation and joint efforts, we must further promote the development of international telecommunications." Deputy Chief Shi (Englishman) said, "We three are now recommended by the company and appointed by the Ministry of Communications, and we will continue to serve in the company's reception and dispatch office. We will naturally do our best to fulfill our duties and work together with all our colleagues to promote the development of international telecommunications."

Scheduled Takeover 152

After the Ministry of Communications negotiated to recover the right to receive and dispatch telegrams for the Sanshui Line Company, the Ministry dispatched Guo Shirong, Section Chief of the Third Section of the Telegraph Administration Department, Wen Yuqing, Director of the International Telegraph Bureau, Sha Shuyun, Section Chief of the Audit Section, and three others as takeover personnel. After contacting the managers of the three companies, it was decided that at 8 a.m. on May 1, the three takeover personnel would meet with the newly appointed chiefs, deputy chiefs, and assistants of the reception and dispatch offices to carry out the takeover.

Declaration 156

To all national organizations, groups, newspapers, and fellow compatriots: The barbaric invaders are increasingly aggressive, having already seized four provinces and now disturbing North China. As our country faces imminent demise, the only way to survive is through unity. Our association held its fourth standing committee meeting in Shanghai on the 29th of this month. After discussion by the attending committee members, it was unanimously agreed that the past internal conflicts have led to today's perilous situation. Therefore, the only way to seek a future path to survival is for the entire nation, from top to bottom, to be of one mind and one heart, to abandon selfish views, to jointly avert the crisis, to resist Japan with all our strength, and to establish domestic peace and construction. At this time and in this situation, there must not only be no more internal conflicts in reality, but also no more imagining of internal conflicts. Not only must there be no more imagining of internal conflicts, but also no more psychological barriers. Only by refraining from certain actions internally can we then take effective actions externally. If we unite our strength, we will succeed; harmony ensures victory. We offer this sincere declaration, hoping that you will consider and accept it. Sincerely, the Abolish Internal War Grand Alliance General Assembly.

Opening a Dock 160

Previously, due to the shipyard's thriving business, the existing No. 1 and No. 2 docks were insufficient. The director personally opened a new dock last year at the West Fort, which is over 600 feet long and can be used to repair large ships, such as the 10,000-ton President steamer. Since the groundbreaking, progress has been hindered by the January 28th Incident, causing delays until now. It is now planned to resume construction in the near future, requiring approximately one million yuan. Xujiahui Merchants and Residents Oppose Stopping Dredging of the Pu Zhao River 164

Since the Shanghai Municipal Government divided the Puzhao River in western Shanghai into sections and invited workers to dredge it, work has now begun in order, and the Songqing section west of Jiepai Bridge will soon be completed. However, the eastern half of the sixth section (i.e., from Pailou Bay to Jinji Bridge) is now facing suspension due to the Municipal Government's tight budget and cost-saving measures. When the merchants and residents of the entire town of Xujiahui learned of this, they were all alarmed. They believe that the river surface of the sixth section is an important waterway for ships traveling between the town and Sijing, and is particularly important for shipping. Yesterday, they jointly submitted a petition to the Rehabilitation Association, the Municipal Government, and the River Dredging Committee, requesting that the dredging be carried out quickly according to the original plan.

Notes on Labor Disputes 165

Hua Shun Rubber Factory

The Hua Shun Rubber Factory on Kang Nai Tuo Road employs more than 100 workers. The factory announced a temporary closure on the 9th of this month, and work has not yet resumed. Due to livelihood concerns, the workers petitioned the party and government agencies on the 24th. However, because no mediation has been convened, yesterday morning at 10:00, representatives Qiu Zemin, Shen Hongsheng, Ni Shunrong, Li Jingui, Cai Ajin, Min Jingen, and others went to the Social Affairs Bureau for a second petition, requesting an early resolution. The mediator Zhang Chuqiang received them and scheduled a meeting for both labor and management at the Social Affairs Bureau on May 1st at 9:00 AM for questioning and mediation.

First Foundry

The Shanghai First Foundry at the end of Kunming Road, Gao Lan Bridge, dismissed two workers on the 20th of this month, causing opposition from the majority of the workers. The workers in the molding department went on strike, demanding the reinstatement of the dismissed workers, which has not yet been resolved. Yesterday morning at 9:00, both labor and management were convened for questioning. Labor representatives Pu Zhixuan, Tang Lindao, Zhang Shenghou, Lu Shunhua, Wu A'er, Yu A'lai, and others arrived, but because the management did not arrive, it was impossible to proceed. Zhu Jintao, a representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, said that the workers' sudden strike due to the dismissal of workers was inappropriate and should be reported to the competent authorities. However, in order to avoid the expansion of the situation, it was rescheduled for both parties to be questioned at the bureau on May 1st at 9:00 AM. The notification has been issued.

Due to the Poor Market Conditions

The depression in Shanghai's business community has reached its peak. In the British and French concessions, newly built municipal houses on various roads are vacant and closed, with no one to rent them. The reason is that the rents are too high, and no one inquires. Huang Gu'en Discusses Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery 167

It is reported that the Ministry of Finance has appointed Zheng Lai as the director of the Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery Office. A certain gentleman visited the office yesterday and was received by Secretary-General Huang Gu'en. The following is a record of his conversation: (Question) I understand the purpose of issuing the lottery from the name, but please provide more details about the measures. (Answer) The government believes that China has a vast territory and a large population, and transportation is very inconvenient. Therefore, it plans to issue this lottery four times a year, with a total value of 5 million yuan each time. Half of the money will be used as prize money for more than 50,000 numbers, 10% will be commission for the sales outlets, 5% will be for issuance and all necessary expenses, and the remaining 35% will be used to develop commercial aviation, such as purchasing airplanes, building airfields and repair shops, and establishing aviation schools. It will also be used to build highways and bridges to facilitate transportation throughout the country and develop agriculture and commerce in the interior. (Question) When will the first phase be issued and drawn, where will it be held, how will the huge amount of 5 million yuan be sold, and how will the prize money be distributed? (Answer) The first phase will be issued in early May, and the draw will be held in Shanghai on July 31st or earlier. The 5 million yuan will be divided into 500,000 lottery tickets, each selling for 10 yuan in Shanghai silver dollars. The office will select political and commercial institutions in various provinces of China, as well as overseas commercial institutions, to act as sales agents and promote sales as much as possible within three months. If there are any remaining tickets unsold at the end of the period, the Ministry of Finance will acknowledge them, regardless of the amount, until the actual amount reaches 5 million yuan. Therefore, the prize money will definitely be paid in full according to the amount. This is the sales method. As for the distribution of the prize money, it is as shown in this table. (When Mr. Huang spoke, he showed the prize money grade distribution table, which is now recorded as follows:

First Prize: 1 ticket, sole winner of 500,000 yuan, total 500,000 yuan

Second Prize: 2 tickets, 100,000 yuan each, total 200,000 yuan

Third Prize: 4 tickets, 50,000 yuan each, total 200,000 yuan

Fourth Prize: 10 tickets, 10,000 yuan each, total 100,000 yuan

Fifth Prize: 50 tickets, 2,000 yuan each, total 100,000 yuan

Sixth Prize: 100 tickets, 500 yuan each, total 50,000 yuan

Seventh Prize: 500 tickets, 200 yuan each, total 100,000 yuan

Last two digits of the first prize number match: 4,999 tickets, 70 yuan each, total 349,930 yuan

Last digit of the first prize number matches: 44,999 tickets, 20 yuan each, total 899,980 yuan

Total winning tickets: 50,665 tickets, total prize money: 2,499,910 yuan

(Question) The issuance of this lottery is handled by your office, but how will the draw be handled? (Answer) The issuance is the responsibility of the office. However, for the sake of seriousness, the National Government has specially established the Aviation and Highway Construction Lottery Committee to be responsible for supervision. Prominent figures from financial, commercial, and industrial circles in Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, the Minister of Transportation, and representatives designated by the Supervisory Yuan, the Accounting Office, and the Ministry of Finance are invited to serve as committee members. However, all committee members are honorary positions only. Therefore, during the draw, the committee will send supervisory members, together with representatives from the Shanghai Local Court, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and the Bankers Association, to supervise the event in order to show seriousness and fairness. (Question) The committee is composed of Chinese and foreign figures, but can you show its powers? (Answer) The powers of the committee are very simple but extremely important, and can be divided into five items: (A) Approving the lottery issuance period and draw date; (B) Supervising the execution of affairs during the lottery draw; (C) Resolving all disputes arising from the lottery; (D) Safekeeping of the lottery proceeds, depositing them at any time in reputable Chinese and foreign banks, and allocating them to the government-designated construction funds; (E) Issuing various checks from the lottery proceeds. (Answer) After the draw, the matching number list is very important. How will it be certified by your office? (Answer) The matching number list will be issued by the office, but it must first be signed by the executive chairman and two members of the Lottery Committee, two notaries, and the office's Chinese accountant Huang Chengzhang and foreign accountant Xue Mailuo for certification. The gentleman excused himself and left due to the late hour.

Shenxin No. 6 Factory Worker Dies Tragically on the Job 168

Wu A'er Loyal to His Duties

Crushed to Death by a Machine

Wu A'er, a 22-year-old worker at the Shenxin No. 6 Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road, originally from Yancheng, was working in the waste cotton room at around 10:00 AM the day before yesterday. Unexpectedly, the belt on the motor suddenly came off and fell to the ground, causing the machine to stop turning while the motor was still running. Upon seeing this, Wu immediately disregarded the danger and attempted to put the belt back on so that the machine could continue working. However, due to carelessness, his sleeve was caught by the belt, which crushed Wu's arm bone and caused severe injuries all over his body. He was bleeding profusely, a gruesome sight. His coworkers Meng Wu Bao and Tang Buyun noticed and immediately stopped the motor and tried to rescue Wu. However, it was too late. He was barely alive. They immediately reported to the factory staff, who reported to the Yangshupu Police Station, ordering detectives to investigate. After the investigation, Wu was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died shortly after. His body was taken to the Feilun Road Coroner's Office. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Zhang Yaoguang was dispatched by the First Special District Local Court to examine the body. He ascended the stand to hear the case. According to Meng Wu Bao and Tang Buyun's testimony of the situation at the time, and according to the victim's mother, Wu Ji Shi, who reported the case, she demanded that the factory provide heavy compensation. The factory sent Zhang Haitang, a staff member of the general affairs department, who agreed to give her 200 yuan in compensation. However, she was still not satisfied and refused to sign the body collection form. Although Prosecutor Zhang explained the reasons with kind words, she did not listen. Mr. Zhang then ruled that the deceased Wu A'er had indeed died from being crushed by the machine wheel. The body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for temporary burial, pending collection.

The Truth About Sheng Xiegui's Escape 169

Absolutely Not Redeemed with a Price

Since Mr. Sheng Xiegui, the Ningbo-born manager of the Yunfei Automobile Company's head office in Shanghai, was kidnapped the day before yesterday (the 27th) and escaped the next day (the 28th), the details of the entire process have been reported in this newspaper twice. However, after the news of Mr. Sheng's escape spread, there was much speculation in the outside world. Some said that Mr. Sheng escaped secretly, while others said that he was redeemed with a considerable price. The rumors were diverse and confusing. This reporter met with Mr. Sheng's close relatives yesterday, who said that Mr. Sheng's escape was definitely not redeemed with a price. The most important reason was that the police's pursuit was urgent, leaving no room for negotiation. Therefore, the bandits released him automatically the next day.

Wu Xinzhi's Two Concubines Agreed to Flee Together 170

Stealing a Lot of Cash and Clothing

One Concubine Suddenly Regretted and Returned

Wu Xin, a 29-year-old Zhejiang native, runs a Samsung Flower Machine Factory at No. 13 Fuxing Lane, Beijing Road. Five years ago, he paid 600 yuan to take a Suzhou prostitute, Cheng Xiuzhen (now 22 years old), as a concubine. Three years ago, he spent 1,600 yuan to take a Hangzhou prostitute, Zhu Baobao (now 20 years old), as his third concubine. They all lived in the factory. Wu had a very harmonious relationship with the two women. The husband and two wives lived in peace. However, on the evening of the 26th of this month, Wu, who also served as a special patrolman, was ordered to go on duty. His bookkeeper, Mr. Shen, received 1,600 yuan in payments and went to hand it over to Wu Xin. Because Wu was not there, he gave it to Cheng to collect on his behalf, so that it could be handed over to Wu. Unexpectedly, Cheng, having obtained a large sum of money, discussed it with Zhu Baobao and suddenly had a bad idea. They stole valuables worth more than 2,000 yuan and fled without a trace. When Wu returned home and discovered what had happened, he reported it to the police and issued a warning. Later, Wu learned that the two women had a close relationship with Wang Jin, the madam of the Mingyue Shuju brothel at No. 3 Fuwu Lane, Guangxi Road. He went to investigate with a detective. When they arrived at the entrance of the brothel, they suddenly heard the voices of Cheng and Zhu talking. They immediately entered to search, but the two women had disappeared. When asked, the people in the brothel also said they did not know. At about 1:00 AM the day before yesterday, Cheng Xiuzhen suddenly returned home and was detained by Wu. When questioned in detail, she said that after escaping, they stayed at the Huizhong Hotel for one night. The next day, they went to Mingyue's place. Unexpectedly, Wu Xin also came to inquire at that time. They hid under the drying rack, so they were not caught. Later, they went to the Oriental Hotel on Xizang Road and lived together in Room 361. Because she made a big mistake, she rashly returned home to atone for her sins. Except for the 200 yuan that was spent, all the stolen items were handed over to Zhu Baobao, who turned them over to her mother for safekeeping, and so on. Wu sent her to the police station, and the detective arrested Zhu Baobao. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Division of the First Special District Local Court. Judge Wu Xiangzu interrogated them. The police lawyer explained the situation and prosecuted them for embezzlement under Article 357 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, Zhu Baobao denied handing over the stolen items to her mother for safekeeping. Judge Wu ordered the two defendants to be detained and rescheduled the trial because the case still needed investigation.

(2) The executive committee members for China and Germany were determined as follows: China: Ye Gongchuo, former Minister of Railways, Liu Haisu, President of the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts, Liang Long, Counselor of the Chinese Embassy in Germany, Geng Dexiang, Secretary of the Chinese Embassy in Germany. Germany: Salf, President of the German East Asian Art Society, Dr. Klemberer, Dr. Kummel, Dr. Giusbery Prof. Balraclunanu, Dr. C8ln, Dr. Reidemeister, Dr. Male, Dr. Liude, Prof. Ammersdorfer. (3) The distribution of financial burdens was determined as follows: 1. The transportation costs of exhibits from China to Hamburg shall be borne by China, and the transportation costs from Hamburg to Berlin shall be borne by Germany. 2. China shall advance 3,000 marks as a subsidy preparation fund for use when the exhibition income is insufficient to cover expenses. At the same time, Germany shall also advance the same amount of subsidy preparation fund. 3. The exhibition items shall be insured for nine months, and the insurance shall not only be limited to Germany, so that they can still be exhibited in other countries after the exhibition in Germany. 4. The German side believes that it is best for all paintings to be rolled. 5. All exhibits must indicate the selling price, so that they can be purchased by admirers after the exhibition. When setting the price, it must be noted that one-tenth of the selling price must be sent to the owner of the exhibition venue (i.e., the Berlin Academy of Art) after the exhibit is sold.

Shanghai-Qidong Shipping Lines Seek Cooperation 173

As a Result of Mediation by the Shipping Association

There are seven merchant ships operating on the Shanghai-Qidong line, including Baofeng, Baohua, Xin Renhe, Guangxiang, Xin Shengda, Fuxing, and Haimen. Since the dissolution of the Public Bureau last autumn, they have been competing by lowering prices, and their businesses have suffered losses. In particular, those with larger hulls and better equipment have shown signs of financial strain due to their higher expenses. It is heard that the Tong, Ru, Chong, Hai, and Qilu Shanghai Fellow Townsmen Association, recognizing that the price reductions by the ships may offer small advantages to passengers and merchants for the time being, predicts that in the future, the companies may be unable to maintain operations due to excessive losses and will be forced to suspend operations. The large ships will inevitably be affected. In the future, only ships with simple equipment and smaller tonnage will operate, and if passengers and goods are crowded and the load is too heavy, dangers will occur. The fellow townsmen of Chongming, Hai, and Qidong counties will bear the brunt of the impact. The lessons of Dalian are not far off. Therefore, they joined forces with the Shipping Association to mediate. After several discussions, there were some signs of progress. The association invited representatives from the governments and chambers of commerce of Chongming, Hai, and Qidong counties, and convened the persons in charge of each company, to hold a mediation meeting at the Shipping Club. Those present included Ding Hongguan (representative of Chongming County Government), Liu Fuchen (representative of Chongming County Chamber of Commerce), Chen Chi (representative of Haimen County Government), Xu Lisheng and Chen Huafu (representatives of Haimen County Chamber of Commerce), Yang Yongyan (representative of Qidong County Government), Gu Yueseng and Jiang Xiangyin (representatives of Qidong County Chamber of Commerce), Lu Caifu, Gu Nanqun, Mao Huiyu, Gu Shaowen (representatives of the Five Counties Fellow Townsmen Association), Chen Bogang (representative of the Shipping Association), and the managers' representatives of each company, totaling more than 20 people. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to establish a joint office for the Shanghai-Qidong shipping industry to unify passenger ticket prices and water freight rates. A board of directors and a board of supervisors will be established, and there will be specific decisions on equipment and treatment. Local government groups will implement supervision to achieve the goal of passenger safety.

(4) Thatched houses will be built at the venue to accommodate the equipment of 120 factories, with room for expansion if necessary. (5) The total cost is estimated at 3,600 yuan, with each room costing approximately 25 yuan. (6) The Chamber of Commerce is responsible for electricity, accommodation, and all arrangements. (6) Various entertainment venues will undertake voluntary publicity. (7) A drama theater and an open-air cinema will be opened in the venue to increase the interest of the guests. After discussion, it was decided to schedule a general meeting of all factory representatives at the Jiumu Di clubhouse at 3:00 PM this (30th) afternoon to discuss measures, begin registration, and elect responsible committee members to actively prepare.

The Shanghai National Products Factory Association sent letters to various factories yesterday, stating that the third Zhejiang Provincial National Products Exhibition is now scheduled to open on May 10th in Hangzhou. Establishment of the Fishery Merchants United Benefit Association 177

Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the Shanghai Fishery Merchants United Benefit Association held its inaugural meeting. Present were Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters representatives Zhang Yinchu and Zhang Sheng, along with 28 other representatives. Chairman Zhou Lianze presided over the meeting, the order of which was as follows: (1) All stood at attention, (2) Paid three bows to the portrait of the Party, the Nation, and the Prime Minister, (3) Respectfully read the Prime Minister's will, (4) Observed a moment of silence, (5) The chairman reported on the preparations, (6) Representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau gave speeches, (7) Proposals were discussed, (8) Elections were held, (9) Newly elected members were sworn in, (10) A group photo was taken, (11) The meeting adjourned. The results of the election were as follows: The elected directors were Zhou Lianze, Chu Genfu, Wu Wenguang, Zhu Yangwu, Shen Mingzhe, Yu Rongqing, Ji Dingfang, Yu Zhu-shi, and Chu Yutang. The alternate directors were Zhang Lansheng, Yu Jiasheng, Zhang Genfa, and Chu Genlong. The elected supervisors were Wu Longsheng, Yao Xingdao, Chen Ganfu, He Zongnian, and Zhu Wenshan. The alternate supervisors were Lu Weixin and Zhang Yuxiu. The proposals of the general meeting were as follows: (1) The fishery construction fee has been collected starting from the 15th of this month, with fresh, salted, and dried products all subject to the levy. In order to protect the interests of inland fresh fish merchants, what measures should the association take? Resolved: Request the Fishery Improvement Association to allow the association to participate in the supervision, custody, and distribution of funds. (2) Fresh river fish boats have always relied on ice-fresh wharves, which has caused them great suffering. How should they raise funds to build a dedicated wharf for fresh river fish? Resolved: Handed over to the board of directors for handling. (3) Member Xia Qiaosheng's boat was overturned by Yuan Xiangxiang's boat, resulting in the drowning of his wife, daughter, and a total of four crew members. What measures should the general meeting take? Resolved: The association will send a letter of condolence to the family. Representative Lu from the Municipal Party Headquarters gave a speech, stating that fresh river fish and ice-fresh fish are the two major fishery industries in Shanghai. Fresh river fish merchants are adhering to outdated methods and should urgently improve them. In the future, rural and urban economies can be harmonized. He hoped that fresh river fish merchants would strive and fight hard, and that the suffering they have experienced can be relieved through organization. Otherwise, the suffering will only deepen day by day. The only thing members lose by joining the association is the membership fee, but the benefits they receive are great. He hoped that everyone would understand the importance of concentrating their strength. All the facilities in the association are the will of the members. Supporting the association is protecting oneself. He hoped that all members would develop close relationships and not treat each other like strangers. The future of the association will surely shine brightly.

Datong Music Society's Second Step of Work 179

Editorial Department ··· Training Institute ··· Manufacturing Department

Since its establishment, the Datong Music Society in this city has compiled a history of Chinese music, manufactured a complete set of musical instruments, and trained an orchestra. Its national endeavors include the National Grand Music, the Zhonghe Shao Music, and the Chinese Military Music. Its artistic endeavors include the Neon Feather Dress Dance, Spring River Flower Moon Night, ensemble and solo performances on the qin, se, konghou, and pipa, as well as various elegant and popular silk and bamboo music. Recently, it has also produced sound films to participate in the Chicago World's Fair. The society believes that the first step of its work has been completed. Now, for the sake of the surrounding environment and to gradually approach Western music, without sufficient preparation, there is still a risk of failure. For this reason, the society has specially made a second step of progress. It is said that there are three prerequisites for its work: (1) Establish a national music editorial department to collect ancient great masterpieces and create new scores suitable for national music. (2) Expand the orchestra and national music normal school training institute. (3) Establish a musical instrument manufacturing department to standardize the national music law. In addition, the promotion of lyrics and melodies is also included, with a three-year completion period. Then, the third step of work will be carried out to combine Chinese and Western music into one furnace to complete the society's initial purpose.

Postponement of Price Increase for Public Concession Park Tickets 180

During the board meeting of the Public Concession on April 26th, a director suggested that the large number of visitors to the parks under the Bureau's management made it difficult to manage, and it seemed appropriate to increase the price of annual tickets from one dollar to two dollars. Another director then suggested increasing the price of retail tickets by two cents each, without increasing the price of annual tickets. After consideration, it was decided to postpone the price increase because the term of the annual tickets was about to expire at the end of May, and the new tickets for the next term had already been printed and were inconvenient to change. However, the matter was handed over to the Works Committee for further consideration.

The Seriousness of the Leprosy Problem in the Yangtze River Basin 181

The Rotary Club of Shanghai recently invited Mr. Wu Zhijian, a Master's degree holder and the General Manager of the China Leprosy Relief Association, to give a lecture on leprosy in the Yangtze River basin. Mr. Wu said that according to expert statistics, there are three million lepers in the world, and China accounts for about one-third of them. This time, he was ordered to inspect Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Jiangbei, and he deeply felt that this disease is indeed a serious social problem in our country. The disease is particularly widespread in the central and southern counties of Hunan, likely because the area is adjacent to Guangdong, and the disease was probably introduced from that province. The northern part of the province has fewer cases. According to expert Mr. Fu Leren, leprosy in Hubei is concentrated on both sides of the Yangtze River and in areas with many lakes. There are also many lepers in Jiangxi, and the disease is spreading rapidly inland. Fortunately, Nanchang has our association's hospital, which helps to alleviate the suffering. Rugao, Dongtai, Yancheng, Qingjiangpu, and other places in northern Jiangsu can be called the center of leprosy. There are also many lepers in Shanghai, mostly from Jiangbei, concentrated in Zhabei, Yangshupu, Xujiahui, and Pudong. At present, our association plans to expand the existing Hongkou Dermatological Hospital to cope with the situation.

Page 14

Reader Consultant

Re-discussing "Can the Countryside Be Returned To?" by You Huaigao 186

Before I discuss this issue, I have a few very sincere words to say to the readers. I strongly disapprove of using sarcastic and harsh language to attack anyone who submits articles. It is a waste of space and achieves nothing. This is not the original intention of the Shen Bao's establishment of the Reader Consultant section. Therefore, I will not only refrain from using retaliatory measures to attack those who have ridiculed and scolded my articles in the past ten days or so, but also advise readers, especially Mr. Liu Siming, to be prudent in discussing and publishing their opinions.

Please understand that the open discussion in the Reader Consultant section is like a round table conference. Shen Bao is the chairman, and we are all members attending the discussion on the question of "Can the Countryside Be Returned To?" We must focus on the question itself in order to reach a conclusion. This is what Mr. Xiongsheng hopes for, and it is also what the readers hope for. Otherwise, straying too far from the topic will make it impossible for everyone to discuss. We are guests invited by Shen Bao, and we should speak politely so as not to lose the demeanor of scholars. Shen Bao provides us with space, and we should make good use of the opportunity to express ourselves as much as possible, because I believe that the current rural problem is indeed a major problem in China, worthy of our careful and meticulous discussion. Therefore, I agree that readers should abandon minor details and focus on the big picture. In my opinion, there should be at least two observations on this issue: (1) How to solve the problem of personal life after returning to the countryside, as asked by Mr. Xiongsheng. (2) How to solve the entire rural problem of the country. The first question has already been answered to Mr. Xiongsheng on April 5th. As for the second question, please allow me to discuss and explain it further.

In the past ten days or so, I have read more than a dozen articles. Very few people agree with the idea of "Can the Countryside Be Returned To?" Some people believe that the countryside is full of imperialist aggression, bandits, warlords, local tyrants, exorbitant interest rates, and heavy taxes. It is almost impossible to live in the countryside for even a day. Unemployed people come to the city to make a living. The countryside is bankrupt. Therefore, if we want to return to the countryside, we must fundamentally transform this distorted social situation. So, unless imperialism is overthrown and capitalism is overturned, even if the countryside becomes as developed as the United States, it will only experience a widespread economic panic like the United States. What good is there in that? This is the argument advocated by people like Mr. Liu Siming and Mr. Zhu Ying. You must understand that China is vast in territory, and you cannot use the special situation of one place at one time to say that the whole country is like that. The poverty of farmers did not begin today. As for saying that all farmers are bankrupt, I am afraid that is an exaggeration. Imperialist aggression is naturally felt most acutely in the city, not in the countryside. Although there are bandits in the countryside, the kidnappers and thieves in the city are much more vicious. There is indeed oppression by local tyrants and bullies in the countryside, but the evil deeds and murders committed by the ruthless tycoons and unscrupulous merchants in the city are probably also much more vicious. The exorbitant interest rates in the countryside are not as bad as the high rents in the city. I do not believe that the heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies in the countryside are more numerous than the stamp duties, business taxes, import and export taxes, house taxes, vehicle taxes, and license taxes in the city. If you say that unemployed people in the countryside have all run to the city, that is not a fact. Even taking Shanghai as an example, it is less than one percent of the number of people in the whole country. I believe that people come to Shanghai to make a fortune, but I doubt that they come to Shanghai to make a living because they are unemployed. Therefore, I say that people who come to the city, except for laborers who do indeed come from the countryside, are only of two types: one is capitalists from the inland, and the other is gangsters from the inland. Both of them want to make a fortune more easily than in the inland. So, instead of saying that the intrusion of imperialism into the countryside has bankrupted the countryside, it is more reasonable to say that the scientificization of foreign agriculture has taken away the Chinese farmers' market, causing the Chinese countryside to go bankrupt and farmers to be impoverished. It is indeed terrible that imperialism uses the sharp weapons of science to secretly kill our compatriots. Look at American cotton, which is longer, better, more abundant, and cheaper than ours. Therefore, the yarn factories in our country buy American cotton instead of domestic cotton. American wheat is larger, whiter, more abundant, and cheaper than ours. Therefore, the flour mills in our country buy American wheat instead of domestic wheat. Siamese rice is better and cheaper than ours. Therefore, the grain merchants in our country buy Siamese rice instead of domestic rice to make up for the shortage. Chinese silk is not as good as Japanese silk. Therefore, the United States buys Japanese silk instead of Chinese silk. The tea market has been mostly taken away by Japan and India. Because Chinese merchants like to adulterate tung oil, the United States has already planted tung trees in the South. Therefore, if China does not fundamentally improve farmers' knowledge through rural education and seek major scientific reforms in agriculture and industry, no matter how hard Chinese farmers work and no matter how thrifty they are, they will never be able to compete with the scientifically advanced agriculture of foreign countries. They will only face failure and elimination day by day. I see through this danger, so I am shouting and advocating a theory of rural education to save the country (10,000 copies of the separate edition have been printed and distributed throughout the country. Please attach a one-cent stamp to send it to you). I do not oppose the government and soldiers' work of resisting Japan and defending the country, but I do not advocate mobilizing the whole country to go to the front line to resist Japan like Mr. Liu Siming. My opinion is that while we are bravely resisting Japan, the people should also do some grassroots work. This grassroots work is for the intellectual class to serve the countryside, to build it in education, agriculture, and social work, because we are at most millions of people. If we shout in the city, and if we leave these hundreds of millions of farmers alone to do the work of construction and resistance against Japan, our strength will be limited. Therefore, the purpose of my theory of rural education to save the country is this. Finally, in this month, I have received more than 100 letters from various places (including three letters from Jiangxi, all wanting to return to the countryside, which is enough to prove that the countryside cannot be returned to is not a fact). After reading them, I almost burst into tears, because the honest and sincere attitude, the patriotic zeal, the sincere desire for knowledge, and the simple desire for improvement in the letters are all enough to make me admire them immensely. I feel that there is hope for China's future. People of conscience should work even harder to save the country. I am very willing to spend a few hours every week, within the possible scope, to discuss with comrades who want to return to the countryside and to correspond with comrades who are already serving in the countryside. All letters will be answered one by one. I would also like to introduce several organizations that have already achieved considerable success in serving the Chinese countryside: one is the Rural Construction Research Institute in Zouping County, Shandong (sponsored by Mr. Liang Shuming), one is the Pingjiao Society in Ding County, Hebei (sponsored by Mr. Yan Yangchu), and the rural undertakings run by the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association in various counties of Hebei and by Jinling University in Wujiang have all achieved considerable success. If all provinces and counties in China can emulate and implement them, there will be hope for the future of the countryside (the discussion of this issue ends).

Cart Drivers Fight for Transportation Business 187

Two People on the Truck Side Injured

Yesterday morning at around 11:00 AM, the head of the Lujinji Brick and Tile Company on Macgregor Road hired manual cart drivers to transport a large batch of bricks and tiles. Traffickers Convicted 190

The Huishan police detective Li Hongsheng and others previously arrested Wang Jiang-shi, Huang Wei-shi, Lu Li-shi (all from Jiangbei), and Wu Asi on the Fujian Maru ship at the Osaka Wharf and at Heda Lane on Baoding Road. They rescued two children, Wang Koubao, six years old, and Jin Dongquan, ten years old, and sent them along with the suspect Huai Qicai to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. The two children were later claimed by their families, Wang Qiu-shi and Jin Qi-shi. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan, along with the Chief Prosecutor, came to Criminal Division No. 3 to continue the interrogation. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the previous situation and questioned Wang Jiang-shi and Huang Wei-shi. They confessed that Wang Laosi, who was on the run at the time, ordered them to watch over the two children on the ship and sell them to Fujian for a reward of ten yuan each. Lu Li-shi confessed that Wang Laosi also ordered her to escort the two children to Fujian. Wu Asi confessed that he had abducted the child Wang Koubao on Changan Road and handed him over to Wang Laosi, receiving two yuan. Huai Qicai confessed that he was an apprentice at Huang Kaiyuan's place, where Huang Wei-shi went, and that he knew nothing about the child abduction. He asked for leniency. Judge Wu then sentenced Wang Jiang-shi, Huang Wei-shi, and Lu Li-shi to three years in prison each, and Wu Asi to four years in prison. The number of days of detention before the final verdict was determined to be equivalent to one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. Huai Qicai was acquitted.

Shot, but Still Indulgent 191

Claimed to be Hit by a Stray Bullet During a Robbery

Found to be a Love Quarrel

At 4:00 PM a few days ago, a man wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants came to Renji Hospital for treatment. He had been shot in the left hand and left foot with a pistol bullet. He claimed that he had been hit by a stray bullet during a robbery near No. 9 Shushengli, Jiudia. The incident was learned by the Laozha police, who sent officers to investigate at the Second District Public Security Bureau. Shen Zhenhua, the head of the Second District First Sub-Bureau, stated that there was no robbery or shooting in Jiudia. Police officer Ma Yumin was also sent to the scene to investigate and found that there was no Shushengli in Jiudia. He then went to Renji Hospital and questioned the injured man again and again. The injured man finally said that his name was Wang Ahai and that he actually lived at No. 19 Shuxingli, opposite the Xiaobeimen in the French Concession. The gunshot wound he suffered was actually due to a love quarrel, and he was shot by an enemy. The injured man has now been taken to the hospital by Detective Zhou from the French police for interrogation, fearing that there may be hidden circumstances, so that they can thoroughly investigate. Police officer Ma has already reported back to the station.

Petty Thugs Pretend to Be Government Employees and Extort Money 192

Xiao Zhimei Conspires to Intimidate

Wang Akun Recognizes the Scheme

Wang Akun, 31 years old, from Shaoxing, makes a living by rowing a boat. A few days ago, he and his wife, Gao-shi, transported a large batch of radishes to Shanghai from their hometown. After selling them, they lodged in room 40 of the Dongfang Hotel in Xiaodongmen. At 11:00 PM the night before last, Wang went out for some business. Soon after, more than ten men, looking fierce, pushed open the door and entered. They asked Gao-shi, "Where did your husband go?" She replied that he had gone out for business and would be back soon. She asked them to wait a moment. The men then sat in the room and waited. Soon after, Wang returned and was immediately greeted by one of the men, who sternly said, "We are public security officers on official business. Where are you from? What are you doing here?" Wang saw that the man was wearing a dark blue serge Zhongshan suit and black glasses, looking very much like a government employee. His tone and manner were stern, so Wang replied that he was from Shaoxing and had come to Shanghai to sell goods. However, one of the men suddenly said, "No, no. They are definitely not good people. We should take them to the police station first and then decide what to do." After saying this, he pulled out a pair of handcuffs from his side and moved forward to handcuff Wang, pretending to do so. Wang then quickly clarified that they were indeed a legally married couple. Another man then came forward, pretending to mediate, and advised Wang to pay 20 yuan to settle the matter, and used various threatening words. At this point, Wang realized that the men had come here with the intention of extorting money, so he immediately refused. By this time, the incident had alarmed the people in the hotel, who came out to investigate. Fearing that something unexpected might happen, the hotel owner quickly went out and called the local patrol police. The men saw their opportunity and scattered and fled. Only one man, the one wearing the Zhongshan suit, was apprehended on the spot and taken back to the First District Second Sub-Bureau along with Wang Akun. During the preliminary hearing by Director Liu, Wang explained the situation and requested a thorough investigation. The man, when questioned, gave his name as Xiao Zhimei, 28 years old, from Fujian. He hesitated in his other answers. After investigation by the police, it was found that Xiao Zhimei was an unemployed petty thug who usually engaged in all kinds of illegal activities. This time, he had even dared to impersonate government employees to extort money from travelers, which was extremely unlawful. He was immediately ordered to prepare a written report and be sent to the bureau for questioning.

Coal Boat Breaks Cable and Capsizes 193

The coal boat of the Xinyi Gong Coal Company, located at the Nichengqiao on Suzhou Creek, hired Xin Arong's coal boat to transport 50 tons of coal the night before last. It was towed to the Datong Wharf in Nanshi to moor, waiting to be unloaded onto the Huaan steamship. Unexpectedly, at 1:30 AM, another large steamship moored at the wharf raised anchor and exited the port. Xin's boat was affected, and the mooring cable broke. At that time, the tide was rising rapidly, and the boat drifted southward. When it floated to the Dongjiadu area, it collided with the anchor chain of a motor fishing boat moored there and capsized. All the coal was submerged at the bottom of the river. Fortunately, there was no one on the boat, so no accident occurred. However, the fishing boat's anchor chain was broken, so the boat also drifted southward. Its stern collided with the bow of the Qing'an warship moored behind it, causing minor damage to the warship. The fishing boat itself was still intact. After the accident, all parties involved reported to the Customs Water Police for record-keeping.
