Publishing World 196

▲Labor Law Special Issue Sells Well Nationwide The Labor Law Special Issue published by the Dongwu Law Journal in Kunshan Road, Shanghai, is 370 pages thick, with hundreds of thousands of words. The writers, such as Sun Xiaomei, Shi Shangkuan, Chen Zongcheng, Li Pingheng, Zhu Shikang, Wang Renlin, and others, are all experts in labor law. In addition to a detailed review of Chinese labor law, the special issue also contains thorough discussions on the labor laws of other countries. In order to promote legal scholarship, the society previously launched a prize-winning essay contest, and the special issue includes a brief outline of the contest, including the topics and stamps. The prize money amounts are 500 yuan, 300 yuan, and 100 yuan. Since its publication, readers have been enthusiastic not only because of its rich content but also because of the hope of winning a prize. Out-of-town bookstores such as the Author's Bookstore, Hui Wentang, and Nanjing Zhengzhong Bookstore, Central Bookstore, etc., are almost overwhelmed with customers.

▲May 1st Labor Day Special Issue of Minsheng The Minsheng Bianyuekan (People's Livelihood Semimonthly), edited and published by the Zhonghua Minsheng Improvement Society, has reached its 16th issue. Tomorrow is May 1st Labor Day, and the journal is publishing a special issue. The writers are mostly specialized scholars, and the content is extremely rich, such as Ma Chaosai's "On Chinese Labor Legislation," Pan Gongzhan's "On Labor Education," Li Tingan's "On Labor Hygiene," Chen Zongcheng's "On the National Labor Conference," Zhu Maocheng's "The Path to Labor Self-Help in China," and Zhu Shikang, Wu Shan, Ying Shugui, Tu Zheyin, Zheng He, and other scholars' specialized essays on various labor welfare undertakings, all of which are valuable works. This issue has increased in length but not in price. The single-copy price is 20 cents, and postage is 5 jiao. Those who wish to read the journal can subscribe for the whole year by sending a letter to the society at 20 Bowuyuan Road, Shanghai. The Zhongwai Bookstore at 90 Avenue Mesnil (corner of Rue Luban) also sells the journal.

▲Dasheng Weekly, Fifth Issue Published The Dasheng Weekly, written by contemporary celebrities, has been published and has reached over ten thousand copies in sales, from the south to the north. From this, it goes without saying that the content of the journal is excellent and has a good influence on readers. Now, the fifth issue of the journal has also been published. Its main items include Ai Yun's "Appetite and Sexual Desire," Gu Fengcheng's "The Significance of the Washington Conference," Zhu Shangwen's "The Problem of Chinese Bandits," Zhu Maocheng's "Impressions of Inspecting European and American Industries," Du Dingyou's "Public Libraries and Adult Education," Dong Shu's "Nurseries in the Shanghai French Concession," Chen Lingyi's "Memoirs of Europe (1)," Hu Huaichen's "Academics and Magic Chambers," Zhou Difei's "Answering a Gentleman's Question on the Issue of Divorce," He Bing's "Fascism and New Italy," Zhu Hongxi's "Remembering Hangzhou and Jiangxi," Zhang Yiping's "Random Notes from Bulezhai," and other famous and valuable works. For the sake of popularity, the annual subscription for 50 issues is priced at only one yuan, including postage. Those who wish to subscribe to the journal should contact the Dasheng Weekly at 191 Rue Carde, Shanghai.

▲Chinese Publishing Monthly, Fifth Issue Published The "Chinese Publishing Monthly" published by the Zhejiang Circulation Library has already published its fifth issue. In addition to classifying and introducing the books published by the publishing industry this month to readers, this issue focuses on library science writings, such as Shu Jiwei's "The Steps of University Library Work" and Gong Baoshan's "Several Prerequisites for the Development of Circulation Libraries," which are valuable masterpieces. In addition, there are detailed introductions of books and newspapers by Sun Fuxi, Ji Qingyi, etc., which are essential reading for libraries and educational groups across the country. The price is 15 cents per copy, and the annual subscription is 1.5 yuan. The local distribution points are the Author's Bookstore on Simalu and the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union Library at 230 Bazilu.

▲Excellent Edition of Jijiu Zhang The best edition of Jijiu Zhang is the Yuyan Hall's Zushi edition. Shen Meisou sought it for many years before finally obtaining it and cherished it exceedingly. Yu Yueyuan's collection is comparable to Shen's edition. It was borrowed by Liang Rengong for years, who praised it endlessly. Now, the two collections are combined and printed for circulation, and Ma Zhanweng's postscript is also obtained, which is rare. It is essential for calligraphers. The Xiling Seal Society, Lili Company, and Author's Bookstore all sell it on behalf. There are not many books left, so purchase quickly. The actual price is one yuan per book, and 20% off for ten or more books. The general wholesale is at 292 Route Pere Robert, Shanghai.

▲Leaping, Issue 305 Released Leaping, Volume 3, Issue 5, has been published, containing Dan Ceng's "Diary of a Madman," Zhao Jiwu's "A Ying," and "Crazy Current" by You Zhi, with over 30,000 words. It is illustrated with Zhang Yingchao's "Shooting," sketches, human body drawings, etc. The Modern Bookstore is the general distributor. The price is 7 cents per copy.

Radio Station 197

▲New Programs on the Sino-Western Radio Station Starting from May 1st, the Sino-Western Pharmacy Broadcasting Radio Station has specially hired the famous novelist Xu Zheshen to tell the "Legend of the Xianghai Knights" in cooperation with Hua Shuju. ▲The Amazing Programs of the Hensen Radio Station Since its opening, the Hensen Wireless Radio Station at 404 Baonanfang, Nanjing Road, has achieved outstanding results. The number of storytelling and ballad programs alone is the best in the Shanghai broadcasting industry. Recently, it has specially hired the famous Suzhou ballad artist Mr. Wang Shouzhang to come to Shanghai, signed a contract, and broadcast exclusively on Hensen. It is heard that it has been scheduled to start on May 1st. From 1:30 PM to 2:30 PM, Wang Shouzhang will sing "Guobao Lu" solo. From 10:00 PM to 11:00 PM, Wang and Fei Yin will partner with Chen Ruilin to perform "Shuangmeng Yuan." Chen Ruilin is good at storytelling, such as "Zhengfan Wobao" and "Jiusi Tao," and has long been famous in the Shanghai broadcasting industry. Wang Shouzhang happens to be his uncle and master, and the book "Wobao" was written by Wang's ancestors. The two gentlemen have a profound family background, and now they are partnering, which will naturally have a complementary effect and add a different color to the Shanghai broadcasting industry.

Miscellaneous News 200

▲Fire Burns Three Sheep Sheds The thatched sheds inhabited by Wang Yu, a native of Teng County, Shandong, near the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway north of Fanhuangdu Creek in western Shanghai, suddenly caught fire at about 3:10 PM yesterday. Immediately, thick smoke filled the air and broke through the roof. Fortunately, it was daytime, and the nearby residents tried their best to put out the fire, which was extinguished. A total of three thatched houses were burned down. The police from the Zhongshan Bridge Police Station in the sixth district were dispatched to detain the fire owner to the sixth district for interrogation.

Letter 203

To Whom It May Concern, According to Zhu Hongru of the Da Xing Company, the news column of Shenbao on April 28 carried a news item about the First Special District Court strictly handling bribery cases, in which the Da Xing Company and Zhu Hongru were involved. The content of the news involved a lawsuit that was actually a matter of the Xie Long Company, and had nothing to do with the Da Xing Company. Da Xing had already transferred the property rights to Xie Long Company, and the Xie Long Company filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court in the name of the owner. There is a record of this. Later, because the lease contained the name of the former owner, Da Xing Company, Xie Long Company changed to using the name of Da Xing Company in the lawsuit in procedure, but in fact and in law, it had nothing to do with Da Xing Company. It has nothing to do with Zhu Hongru of Da Xing Company. Fortunately, it is recently heard that the court is investigating the case, and the facts will not be difficult to come to light in the future. I am afraid that the outside world does not know the truth, and that misinformation will hinder the reputation of Da Xing Company and Zhu Hongru. I have entrusted your lawyer to publish a statement in the newspaper and to write to Shen Xin Erbao to correct the news published on April 28. In light of the above, please make a factual correction. Sincerely, Jiang Jiemin, Lawyer, April 29.

Weather Report 204

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the low pressure in northern Manchuria is moving northeastward. The strong southerly wind on the Bohai Sea will turn into a southwest wind and gradually decrease in strength. The air pressure in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River is low, while the middle and lower reaches will be cloudy with a slight southwest wind. The wind is light and directionless in the East China Sea and the southern Yellow Sea. Also, within the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was 72.5 degrees highest and 52.0 degrees lowest. On the same day last year, the temperature was 64.2 degrees highest and 55.8 degrees lowest.

Education News

Shanghai Citywide Middle School Joint Sports Meet Closed Yesterday, Guanghua Affiliated Middle School Won Four Championships 205

Boys' A and B Group Teams and Individuals All Went to Guanghua

Dong Yinchu for Boys' A Individual, Liu Chongli for Boys' B Individual

Wuben Won the Middle School A Group Championship, Girls' B Undecided

Xiao Jieying for Girls' A Individual, Tan Shangzhen and Guan Yanqiao for Girls' B Individual

The second Shanghai Citywide Middle School Joint Sports Meet, which was once extremely grand, closed satisfactorily yesterday. Guanghua Affiliated Middle School won the double team championships, with 31 points for the Boys' A group and 53 points for the Boys' B group. The individual championships for Boys' A and B also fell into Guanghua's hands, with Dong Yinchu winning 10 points for Boys' A and Liu Chongli winning 15 points for Boys' B. It can be said that it is extremely glorious and commendable for one school to win four championships. Wuben Girls' Middle School won the Girls' A group team championship with 24 points. The Girls' B group team championship has not yet been resolved due to a problem with the high jump event. It will be won by Wuben or Aiguo. The Girls' A group individual championship went to Xiao Jieying of Wuben, with 10 points. The Girls' B group individual championship will be won jointly by Tan Shangzhen of Wuben and Guan Yanqiao of Aiguo, as they each scored 10 points. During the three-day conference, a total of nine previous records were broken and two previous records were tied, which is especially gratifying. Due to lack of time, the award ceremony will be held by the Municipal Education Bureau at a later date.

Yesterday's Grand Occasion 206

Yesterday was the third and final day of the conference. A few drops of rain fell lightly in the morning, but by noon, the sky suddenly cleared up, as if the heavens were completing a beautiful event. The climate was even more comfortable, and the grand occasion of the spectators did not diminish from the previous two days. Because all the competitions were finals, the athletes from each school competed with each other with the spirit of winning the championship in a short battle. The Boy Scouts also worked very hard to serve the public, which is commendable.

Girls' B Team Championship Still Problematic 211

▲Wuben and Aiguo Still Need to Compete

▲Due to Unresolved High Jump

Wuben Holds Advantage, Aiguo Still Has Hope

According to the report of the chief referee, the team championship of the Girls' B group still has problems with the high jump event, which needs to be resolved at a later date, so it cannot be determined at present. However, it will definitely be one of Wuben and Aiguo schools. The scores already obtained by the two schools are: Wuben 24 points, Aiguo 23 points. The situation is described as follows:

Wuben: Wuben has Ji Shuren and Hua Shuzhen in the unresolved high jump. If they can get second and third place after re-jumping, or if one of them gets first place, then 24 plus 5 points equals 29, and Wuben wins the championship. If they get second and fourth place, and Zhang Minzhi of Aiguo gets first place, then the championship will be transferred to Aiguo.

Aiguo: Although Aiguo is currently behind Wuben by one point, if Zhang Minzhi of Aiguo can win first place in the re-jump, then Aiguo will win the championship. Aiguo still has hope, and it is hoped that they will work hard at that time.

Spring and Autumn

Wu Yan's "Little Brother" 226

— Zhan Lu

Someone asked: In Wu dialect, a child is called "Little Gan," how should the character "Gan" be interpreted? I said: "Little Gan" is "Little Brother." "Ge" and "Gan" are transformations of the same sound, easily misread. Here's proof: Wu people call "one" "Yi Gan Zi". Therefore, calling "Little Brother" "Little Gan" is a similar proportional expression, nothing unusual. Someone asked: "Little Gan" is "Little Brother," that's true, but sometimes Wu people call a child "Little Gan Wu," how should this "Wu" be interpreted? I said: "Little Gan Wu" is "Little Brother Er". The "Er" sound is very common in Hangzhou dialect. Wu people are not used to retroflex sounds, so when saying "Little Brother Er," the "Ge" is read as "Gan," and the "Er" at the end of the word is read as the nasal "Wu". -- "Wu" as in the final sound of the English letter N.

Someone asked: In Wu dialect, the "Er" sound is often read as "Ni," like "Er Zi" (son) read as "Ni Zi." Following this logic, "Little Brother Er" should be read as "Xiao Ni Gan," not "Xiao Gan Wu." I said: Wu people have two ways of reading the "Er" sound. When "Er" means "son," it's read as "Wu." When "Er" is at the end of a word and has no meaning, then the "Er" is not read as "Wu," but as the nasal "Wu."

Someone asked: Do you have any evidence to prove that the "Er" at the end of a word is always read as "Wu" by Wu people? I said: Of course, but there aren't many examples. Why? Because Wu people often prefer using "Zi" rather than "Er" at the end of a word. For example, "Mao Er" (hat), "Xie Er" (shoe), "Bei Er" (cup), "Pen Er" (basin), Wu people simply say "Mao Zi," "Xie Zi," "Bei Zi," "Pen Zi," avoiding the retroflex "Er" sound. However, sometimes it's unavoidable, so they have to read "Er" as "Wu." Here are three examples: Wu people call "Ao Er" (padded jacket) "Ao Wu," "Kuai Er" (chopsticks) "Kuai Wu," and "Tao Qu Er" (seeking fun) "Tao Qu Wu." Therefore, Wu people calling "Little Brother Er" "Little Gan Wu" is a similar proportional expression, nothing unusual.

Since we know "Little Gan" is "Little Brother Er," then "Little Wu" is "Little Girl Er," which can be inferred and doesn't need further explanation.

Messages That Cannot Be Disclosed 227

— Zhang Zhenxiang

丨Like the Spring Scenery Filling the Garden, Impossible to Confine丨

People generally believe that newspaper reporters are the least able to keep secrets. Therefore, when there is any secret message, they are deeply afraid of being known by newspaper reporters. Within the realm of possibility, they always try to hide it from the eyes and ears of reporters. If it is impossible to do so, and the facts cannot be hidden, they will not hesitate to use threats and inducements, or gentle requests, bringing out the final means to achieve the goal of not disclosing it in the newspaper. In fact, "If you don't want people to know, don't do it yourself"; this is an unbreakable truth. Although it is possible to prevent these newspapers in this place from publishing it, it cannot be guaranteed in another place. There are other newspapers that recklessly publicize it arbitrarily! Look at the news that Chinese newspapers cannot disclose; isn't it often specially published in foreign newspapers? The more people want to keep something secret, the more it arouses the curiosity of others and promotes people's attention. After all, it cannot be hidden or concealed. This is just like "Spring is filling the garden, impossible to confine, a branch of red apricot extends beyond the wall", the same principle.

Unless the red apricot has never been exposed to the spring breeze, if it has already experienced the spring breeze, and still hopes to maintain its old state, without change, without attracting attention, then it is simply an unreasonable dream! Even if you can find a way to raise the garden wall, not allowing any branches to develop outside the wall, and not allowing the slightest leakage of spring light; however, the spring breeze that cannot be confined still has the "skill of stealing fragrance." Who can stop the spring breeze from having a relationship with the red apricot? Who can deny that the fragrance of flowers cannot be brought out of the garden by the spring breeze?

In the past, it seems that an important person said, "Our good deeds are often hindered, and most of the spring scenery is leaked by newspaper reporters!" According to the speaker's opinion, reporters have become one of the contemporary devils, wishing they could be wiped out in one fell swoop to have the hope of "completing" the so-called "good deeds." In fact, who is the devil? Who is not the devil? If the devil himself has never looked at his face in the mirror, how can he distinguish clearly? If you want the red apricot not to be seen by people outside the wall, then unless the red apricot itself does not secretly embrace the spring breeze! As the saying goes, "Good deeds don't hide from people, hiding them means they are not good deeds." The relationship between the red apricot and the spring breeze has already become an open secret, so there is no need to cover it up again. If the red apricot itself has a need to fear people, then the real devil, we can boldly say, is not someone else, but the red apricot itself!

The Slogan of National Extinction 228

— Zhong Huan

In recent years, the most fashionable slogan in Shanghai, which can be heard everywhere, is "Don't

take it to heart." For example, the sacred laborers say, "Don't take work to heart," the shop clerks say, "Don't take business to heart," the students in schools say, "Don't take schoolwork to heart." Our people, regarding their due obligations, everything, everyone shouts "Don't take it to heart." However, recalling since "September 18th," our government has repeatedly announced to us "long-term resistance," but our army retreated without a fight. Witnessing the beautiful rivers and mountains being taken away by the enemy, with Peiping and Tientsin in imminent danger of not being protected, and the exorbitant taxes and levies

, the money extracted from us is used to feed them, to ensure that they are conscienceless and mad, willing to abandon the tens of millions of miles of resource-rich "Northeast"? I think they are probably also shouting there, "If the Guanwai is lost, don't take it to heart." In the future, "If the Yellow River is lost, still don't take it to heart." Even if the Yangtze River and the Pearl River basins are all lost, everyone will still shout, "Don't take it to heart." Alas! "Even if we become slaves to a conquered nation, don't take it to heart!"

Two Children 229

— Li Houying

It was a rainy day, and there were fewer pedestrians on the road; however, the sidewalks on both sides seemed even more

crowded.

At the corner of the road, at the entrance of a small alley, many people were gathered in a circle, watching the excitement.

This was a place where the rain did not fall, so there were even more people: breaking them down, most were idle people, and a small part were people with unimportant business; I was one of them.

The circle of people on the outside was very large, but the area inside was very small: there was only an empty space of about six or seven feet in diameter, and the protagonists were two children.

A two- or three-foot-long, very dirty cloth was spread on this open space; it was covered with two bowls; there were also three red cloth knots.

The two children were sitting behind this cloth. An older child, about eight or nine years old, cleverly moved the red cloth knots around under the bowls; the other one, even younger, only about seven years old, was also holding a gong, hitting it "Dang dang dang."

The sound of the gong attracted people walking outside; the small magic trick with the three red cloth knots was able to temporarily attract the viewers. Although they were young, they already understood the spirit of cooperation.

Suddenly, the gong stopped, and the magic trick was over; the younger one walked out two steps, and tumbled continuously in the open space. Although it was said to be spring; the weather was still very cold, and they were only wearing a very thin cloth shirt, and the shorts below were also short enough to be above the knees.

After a while, the older one also came out. The two of them hugged each other, connecting with each other and tumbling. Several of the viewers praised, saying, "It's really not easy to earn a few pennies, look how hard they are working!"

After another while, the younger one curled up into a ball, and the older one stood on his stomach. Several of the old customers who watched the free show had already quietly slipped away

good luck; by the time the older child opened his mouth to ask for money, there were only a few people left!

Several people threw down a few coins and left, but I was still standing on the side; suddenly, a police officer came over and drove them away fiercely.

The drizzle had stopped, and the sky was much brighter than before. I wandered along the road, feeling somewhat lost; a kind of lonely and cool gong sound still vaguely lingered in my heart.

Long Novel

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 230

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five: Brewing Tea to Pass the Long Night, Sorrowfully Remembering the End of the Year; Raising the Banner of Resistance, Shouts Resound High

Just like that, it stirred up Jiang's worries. She brewed another pot of tea and sat by the stove, slowly pondering the mixed feelings. She didn't know how long she had been sitting quietly. The girl was already asleep. She thought for a long time and then looked at the girl lying on the kang. She thought that talents like Company Commander Zhao couldn't be considered bad. She didn't understand what her girl meant. She didn't want to marry this relative. Before, it could be said that because of Gan Er Ye, she didn't want anyone else. Now he and Gan Er Ye have broken up, so why is she still unwilling to marry Company Commander Zhao? Jiang quietly thought for half the night but couldn't come to a conclusion. But her appreciation for Company Commander Zhao deepened because of this. On the next day, New Year's Day, she paid even more attention to whether Zhao Ziqiang had returned. But she waited all day without seeing his shadow. On the second day, before she got up, she heard him shouting outside the window: "Has Old Lady Yang gotten up? I'm here to wish you a happy New Year." Jiang smiled and said repeatedly: "I wouldn't dare, I wouldn't dare. I'll come to wish you a happy New Year in a moment." So Zhao Ziqiang left. Jiang, receiving this New Year's greeting from him, didn't know where her happiness came from. She immediately put on her clothes, got off the kang, quickly washed her face, combed her hair, and followed him to the inner courtyard. She saw two people in military uniforms sitting in Zhao Weng's house. Although Jiang recognized Zhao Ziqiang, she was always a little afraid of soldiers, so she stood at the door, taking two steps back. Zhao Ziqiang rushed forward and introduced: "This is Company Commander Yin, this is Company Commander Tian, they are all my sworn brothers." The two company commanders stood up and saluted. Jiang saw that they had guests and didn't want to stay long. She stood there, said a New Year's greeting to Zhao Weng, and left. Company Commander Yin, named Deren, smiled and said: "No wonder Ziqiang said this old lady is kind. Look at her face, it's full of kindness." Company Commander Tian, named Qing, was a young man in his early twenties. His military uniform was exceptionally neat, without a single wrinkle. A pair of leggings was tightly wrapped around his legs, as if glued to his calves. A pair of yellow leather shoes didn't have a speck of dust. Just looking at the fountain pen inserted in his military uniform pocket, he showed the civilization of a military man in his attire. (57)

Children's Paradise

A Duck's Body Is Always Dry 231

A duck's feathers are always dry and don't get

wet. Why is that? Because near the duck's buttocks, there is a gland that secretes oil. Ducks often use their beaks to smear this oil on their bodies, so when ducks swim in the water, they won't get wet, and when they come out of the water, they always shake their bodies to brush the water off their feathers very cleanly.

The Danger of Toys 232

Paper contains a lot of hydrogen and carbon. Celluloid, used for making toys, is a mixture of nitrated cotton and camphor. Since its invention by the American Hayswood in 1865, it has been used to make decorations, daily necessities, toys, photographic plates, etc. Simply put, it's like adding nitric acid to paper. Therefore, the toys we play with will catch fire when exposed to the sun's high heat.

The Skill of Hunting Fish 233

There is a freshwater fish called the Archerfish in East India, also known as the water jet fish. It is about twenty inches long and often hides by the water's edge, waiting for insects. If insects fly and gather on the grass by the water's edge, it slowly raises its head above the water, opens its mouth, and blows out a stream of water, forcefully shooting at the insect's body. When the insect is hit, it falls onto the water's surface, where the fish can swallow it.

The Skin of Frogs 234

Frogs' skin often secretes a sticky liquid. Why is that? Because their bodies don't have feathers, scales, or armor. The sticky liquid can prevent their body temperature from evaporating. If their skin dries out in the strong sunlight, they cannot survive.

Chicken 235

This year is You, You matches the chicken. Therefore, I will make various interesting chicken toys for you to see. The method is very simple. Not only can elementary school students make them, but even younger siblings in kindergarten can also make them. (1) Taro Chicken: Let's get two raw taro, one large and one small. The large one is the chicken body, the small one is the chicken head. Then use matchsticks or wire to connect the head and body. Cut two slices of carrot for the chicken feet to serve as a stand. The chicken's beak and claws are made of carrot flesh. The chicken's eyes are made of nandina seeds or the head of a matchstick. If you look at the picture, you will understand clearly. (2) Flannel Chicken: This chicken is made of scraps of flannel. First, cut out two pieces of white flannel of the same size. Use a pencil to draw the chicken body according to the pattern and cut it out. Then sew a dashed line around the edge (leaving a part of the abdomen unsewn). Sew along the dashed line with a needle. Turn it out from the unsewn area of the abdomen. Fill the inside with cotton. Then use wire to make two feet and insert them into the abdomen. Sew the abdomen closed with thread. Then cut out red flannel to make the chicken's comb and tail. Glue them on with glue, or sew them on with thread (two layers thick). Wrap the wire for the feet with brown wool yarn. The chicken's beak can be painted yellow. The chicken's eyes can be small, round, bean-like buttons, or they can be painted.

— Chu

Free Talk

Further Discussion on "Returning to the Countryside" 236

— Xuan

Regarding Mr. Cao Juren's argument "advocating returning to the countryside," I agree with Mr. Yang Xingzhi's rebuttal. Now I'll say a few more words.

I find it very strange that Mr. Cao divides the Chinese countryside into three types. Mr. Yang has already pointed out that Mr. Cao also errs in "forcibly dividing the entire capitalist world, the entire colonies, and the entire countryside in a state of collapse into two unconnected regions that seem to be independent: : :" However, I think even if we take a step back and examine Mr. Cao's statement out of context, it is still incomprehensible.

First, Mr. Cao said that the areas around Henan and Shaanxi have long become "villages without agriculture." I don't know if the word "agriculture" here refers to "farmers" or "agricultural affairs?" According to Mr. Cao's statement that "the county magistrate orders the planting of tobacco, and those who cannot pay the tobacco tax are beaten on the buttocks," then what he calls "without agriculture" is actually that farmers cannot grow crops, not that there are no farmers. And Mr. Cao then concludes: "Of course, there is no way to return to such villages without agriculture." This is to say: since you cannot farm, what's the point of going back! But doesn't Mr. Cao also advocate going to Type C villages to "organize self-cultivating farmers to fight a self-defense war"? Since you can go to Type C villages to fight a "self-defense war," why is there "of course no way to return" to the so-called "villages without agriculture" of Type A? Are the farmers in Henan and Shaanxi who have land but cannot grow rice truly doomed to die?

Second, Mr. Cao believes that in the areas around Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, and Anhui, capitalism eats the large landlords, and the large landlords eat the tenant farmers. There is "no way to return to this kind of countryside that is on the verge of collapse." Here, Mr. Cao's phrase "countryside on the verge of collapse" is again very ambiguous. If we say that the "rural economy" is on the verge of collapse, then the result of "capitalism eating the large landlords, and the large landlords eating the tenant farmers" is not necessarily the collapse of the "rural economy," but rather the transformation of self-cultivating farmers into serfs. Mr. Cao's meaning may lie in this, so he consistently uses the same perspective for dealing with Type A villages to deal with this Type B village: "there is no way to return either!"

Therefore, he believes that only Type C villages are worth or "have a way" to return to. Because they are centered on self-cultivating farmers, and "they can win even without fighting." However, what a "Utopian" theory this is! However, at the same time, we can also know that Mr. Cao feels that there is "no way to return" to Type A and Type B villages because there are no self-cultivating farmers in those two types of villages, and the power of the gentry and ruffians is very strong. To regard self-cultivating farmers as the basic force in the countryside to resist evil forces is also a misidentification on Mr. Cao's part.

Originally, the short article I published last time only posed negative questions about the calls for "returning to the countryside" in the film City Lights and other three works. I am not advocating not returning to the countryside. As for what to do when returning to the countryside, it's a long story. I can only avoid discussing it today.

Go Back to the Countryside and Do This! 237

— Cao Juren

丨Reply to Mr. Yang Xingzhi丨

The current clamorous issue of returning to the countryside does indeed have a strong Utopian flavor. My advocacy for returning to the countryside is not the same as those who dream of utopia. I myself am a small farmer. I only want to awaken the youth who come from the countryside to return to the countryside. What I said in the previous article only proves that there are still villages to return to, not that everyone must return to the countryside.

In the eyes of us small farmers, nine out of ten of those who loudly shout about returning to the countryside don't dare to "trouble" themselves. What will they do when they go to our villages? Can they feed cattle? Can they cut grass? If they can't even lead cattle or cut grass, what will they do in the countryside? If they say they're going back to be gentlemen, then please stay in Shanghai and "play mahjong," "act wildly with beautiful women," and fill in liberation lyrics! To be honest, none of the young people who have received a university education in Shanghai are qualified to return to the countryside! In the ninth year of the Republic of China, a wave of utopian work-study mutual aid groups arose in Beijing. Tianjin, Jinan, Shanghai, and Hangzhou followed with this kind of organization. Soon, this beautiful soap bubble burst, and nothing was left! If you are tired of urban life and want to go to the countryside to live a idyllic life, then its comical absurdity will of course be the same as that of the work-study mutual aid groups.

However, it is imperative that we return to the countryside, and it is a matter of current importance. The mouth of capitalism is just about to open and swallow up the self-cultivating farmers (please refer to the letter of weeping complaint from more than a thousand tenant farmers of the Yuhua Reclamation Company in Dongtai County to party and government agencies and organizations in Shen Bao on April 27). We urgently need to awaken the self-cultivating farmers and reject their investment. We will organize production and consumption cooperatives, improve agricultural tools, seeds, and promote agricultural products for self-cultivating farmers. Further, we will popularize farmer education, strengthen farmer organizations, and participate in the foundational work of the new society. There are at least tens of millions of self-cultivating households in China. This is not a negligible number, nor is it a negligible force. That is why I say that we will not be too disappointed when we return to the countryside.

However, young people who return to the countryside must possess three qualifications: A, be from a farming background, without the ambition to become a small or large landlord; B, be familiar with new agricultural tool technology and be able to work in the fields with self-cultivating farmers; C, be committed to lifelong service, without any thoughts of seizing power. Most importantly, they must have a strong organization (individuals have no power).

Throughout Chinese history, social movements have only been superficial movements based on slogans, never reaching the people. Can a house on the sand withstand a storm? What I hope for now is that everyone will do the opposite, not rushing for quick results, but burying their heads and focusing on underground movements, and see what our results will be in ten or twenty years. I call this kind of work the "tree planting movement" - 丨a movement that only plants trees for future generations, not wanting to enjoy the shade themselves.

Editor's note: The issue of "returning to the countryside" has been discussed for a long time in this newspaper's Readers' Advisory Column and has not yet ended. After publishing the articles by Mr. Xuan and Mr. Yang the other day, this attracted Mr. Cao's defense. In recent days, we have received many submissions regarding this issue, which has greatly expanded the battle lines. However, this publication has limited space, and it is really inconvenient to publish too much discussion on specialized issues. We are publishing the articles by Mr. Xuan and Mr. Cao, who represent the two sides' opinions, as a conclusion to this.

Deceased Child 238

— En Ping

In the spring, the weather is clear and bright one moment, and then rainy and windy the next, truly the most unpredictable time of year in terms of cold and heat. It was in this kind of capricious weather that the lively and lovely Jieping died at a young age. By May 12th of this year, it will be a full year since Ping'er and I parted forever. She was only two years, two months, and twenty days old when she died, but in this short life, she heard the gunfire of the Sino-Japanese War, saw enemy bombers flying in formation and attacking, and saw the blazing light that burned incessantly day and night in Zhabei. She once followed her mother on an inland river steamer on the Suzhou Creek to avoid the war and return to her hometown, and she also followed her mother on a Yangtze River steamer back to Shanghai. She fell ill three days after returning to Shanghai. I remember on the day of "September 5th Memorial" last year, the signing of the Shanghai Armistice Agreement, it was as hot and cold as this spring. At that time, although her illness had improved, she had not fully recovered her health. Therefore, she caught a cold due to a sudden cold snap one night, and her fragile little body started to have chills and fever again. The illness became more and more serious day by day. After being sent to Guangren Hospital, she changed from chronic pneumonia to acute pneumonia and died after being hospitalized for only three days. This was the first time I felt the horror of death, the cruelty of death! The indescribable pain she endured on the sickbed during those three days is deeply imprinted in my heart and will never be forgotten.

Since Ping'er's death, I have felt the loneliness and solitude of life that cannot be filled. People who have lived in the city of Shanghai for a long time do not easily hear the cuckoo's call, and even if they do hear it occasionally, it is not easy to arouse special feelings. I don't know why, but since Ping'er's death, I have always heard the faint, fluttering cuckoo crying sharply and tragically in the sky. From late spring to early autumn, I heard the cry of "kugu, kugu" almost every day, hearing it on sunny days and hearing it on rainy days. Therefore, I fantasized that this might be Ping'er's spirit, a spirit that had lost its reliance. Sometimes I would go to the balcony, concentrate and listen, following the sound, and stretch my neck to look. Sometimes it sounded as if it were not far away, as if it were on the lush branches in the neighbor's garden; sometimes it seemed very far away, as if it were in the clear blue sky. I recalled my childhood when I lived in the countryside with my grandmother. My eighth younger brother died when he was two or three years old. In a dream, I suddenly saw the small coffin being carried to the ancestral tomb in the countryside for burial. At that time, I also heard the cry of "brother is going home," "brother is going home." I never thought that I would hear the tragic cry of the cuckoo in Shanghai that I had heard in the countryside twenty years ago!

Galsworthy's Literary Harvest 239

— Kagawa

Among world-renowned literary figures who live by their pens, it is said that George Bernard Shaw, who visited China not long ago, has the highest income. But if we investigate the late British literary veteran John Galsworthy, we find that his literary harvest is also quite impressive. According to recently released figures, from the age of forty-five or forty-six to sixty-six, over a period of twenty years, his annual income from royalties on novels and plays, as well as performance fees, totaled between £15,000 and £20,000. Adding to this the fees for short essays and articles contributed to newspapers and magazines in England and America, the total was actually as much as £50,000. Combined with the aforementioned royalties, the total annual income was approximately £70,000. If we take each pound as equivalent to 20 Shanghai circulating dollars, that would be 1.4 million dollars!

Since his income after achieving fame was so high, his work that brought him fame must have sold very well. Consider his representative work, "The Forsyte Saga," the first part of which, "The Man of Property," was published in 1906. In England alone, it quickly sold 100,000 copies. At that time, the author's royalty was 7%, so from this one book alone, he received £7,000 in royalties. As for the entire "Forsyte Saga," it sold 250,000 copies in England, and a total of 500,000 copies in the United States, Germany, and Scandinavia. The income from this is naturally imaginable.

When he reached the age of sixty, he was still energetic and continued to bury himself in writing. I will translate a few words he wrote on his sixty-second birthday here as a conclusion: "The reason I seem younger than those old men is because I practice riding, playing tennis, playing golf, and other sports every day. My creed is health first. My habit of doing things recently is to write novels in the morning, write plays in the afternoon, and absolutely not write in the evening."

Carrot Top 240

— Written by Jules Renard, Translated by Lin Qu

Hoe

Big brother Felix and Carrot Top were working side by side. Each person held a hoe. Big brother Felix's hoe was made of iron by the blacksmith according to measurements. Carrot Top's was made of wood by himself. They were engaged in gardening, working quickly, showing enthusiasm. Suddenly, when Carrot Top was completely off guard (all misfortunes always befall at this time), he was struck on the forehead by a hoe.

A moment later, everyone carried big brother Felix inside, carefully placing him on the bed, because he fainted after seeing his little brother bleed. The whole family gathered there, walking on tiptoes, sighing, and worrying.

"Where is the salt?"

"Please bring some cold water to wet his temples."

Carrot Top climbed onto a chair, peering over the shoulders of others in the crowd. His forehead was wrapped in a cloth, which had already turned red, blood soaking into the cloth and spreading out.

Lepic said to him:

"You got what you deserved!"

His sister Ernestine, who was bandaging his wound, continued:

"It's really like digging in butter."

He didn't cry out, because based on experience, he knew that crying out was useless.

But at this moment, big brother Felix opened one eye, then opened the other. He was no longer afraid, and his face gradually returned to normal, so everyone was relieved.

"It's always like this!" Lepic's family said to Carrot Top: "Can't you be more careful, you idiot!"

Shotgun

Lepic said to his two sons:

"One shotgun is enough for both of you. Loving brothers can share everything."

"That's right, Dad," big brother Felix replied, "We can share one shotgun. And it's enough as long as Carrot Top sometimes lends it to me."

Carrot Top neither said yes nor no, he knew it was unreliable.

Lepic pulled the shotgun out of the green gun case and asked:

"Which of you two should take it first? It seems that the older one should take it first."

"I'm willing to give this honor to Carrot Top. Let him take it first!" big brother Felix said.

"Felix, your behavior today is very polite, I won't forget this," Lepic said.

Lepic then placed the shotgun on Carrot Top's shoulder.

"Go on, you can play well, don't quarrel."

"Shouldn't we bring the dog?" Carrot Top asked.

"No need. You can take turns being the dog yourselves. And, hunters like you won't wound, you'll only kill."

(To be continued)

Finance: US Senate Passes Inflation Bill 241

Causing a Rush for $16.50 Silver

Speculative Interest Wanes, Limited Scope for Rise

The fall in the silver market yesterday was mainly due to the US Senate passing the entire inflation amendment. Selling activity ensued. Initial telegrams from abroad reported that London's spot silver price decreased by 1.875, and the forward price by 25. New York silver prices decreased by a small 0.75, and US cotton also fell by 9 points. However, the forward silver price on the metal exchange rose by 0.5 to 1 penny. Private telegrams increased by 0.0625, and British-US exchange rates increased by 1/4 of 1.25. US-UK exchange rates also rose by 7/21. The opening price for raw silver futures showed a slight decrease, at 47.8 yuan, because the foreign telegrams had not yet arrived. When Reuters reported that the inflation bill had been completely passed, specifying the news from Washington at 7 o'clock (the exchange had already closed, so there was no sign of silver prices rising), people panicked. Hengyu, Ruixing, Fuchang, Hengxing, Qingfa, Yongbingxing, Yuanmao Yong (on behalf of Bingxing) all sold silver bars, and the opening price immediately dropped to 936.5 yuan. The foreign exchange market was flat for British currency and loose for US currency, with little trading. The silver market was also very quiet, with little fluctuation. Reuters telegrams received near noon transmitted the entire inflation amendment, including the provision allowing debtor nations to use silver to repay war debts (up to US$200 million), reducing the gold content by 50%, and allowing free coinage of silver. These provisions were unfavorable to the gold market. The closing price retreated to 933.5 yuan. The spot price premium was increased to 37 yuan, and the swap spread for May and June was 26 yuan. Amendments to the Cotton Delivery Inspection Rules of the Yarn Exchange 254

The cotton delivery inspection rules of the yarn exchange have been amended this month and will take effect in October. The following is a summary: (1) All cotton for delivery shall be inspected by the delivery broker after the 15th of each month and up to three days before delivery. (2) When the cotton is inspected, if the grade and standard are consistent, each 100 dan shall be in about 12 burlap bags, about 85 bags per lot, with four sample flowers, each weighing about one pound (etc.). If it is a large machine-packed bale of about 4 dan, about 25 to 27 bags per lot, totaling 100 dan, two bags must be opened for sampling, and two sample flowers must be taken, each weighing about two pounds. If there are two brands in one lot, two more bags should be opened and two more flowers should be taken for separate inspection of the amount of moisture. (3) The moisture content of the cotton shall be 12%, if it is 13%, the price shall be reduced by 1%, and if it exceeds 13%, it shall be deemed unqualified. (4) Cotton of any packaging may be delivered, but unqualified cotton shall be replaced by the deliverer as soon as possible, and shall be delivered by the day before delivery at the latest. If the inspection is still unqualified, and the delivery cannot be made the next day, it shall be deemed a breach of contract. Qualified products shall be given an inspection certificate, which shall be valid for seven days after the delivery of the month. If the owner considers it inappropriate, they may state the reasons and request a re-inspection. If the inspected cotton is not delivered, a water inspection fee of 3 silver yuan per dan and a weighing fee of 3 silver yuan shall be charged. (5) Delivery shall be in units of 100 dan. If there are four or five dan more or less, it shall be calculated according to the delivery price. When delivering cotton, the stack rent and insurance period must have a surplus of more than two days to be considered qualified (if the warehouse is closed, the period may be extended accordingly). All machine species insurance fees shall be paid by the receiver as usual for the convenience of shipment. (6) The receiver of the delivered goods must clear the goods within two days after the delivery date. If the dock receipt has not arrived, the goods must be cleared within two days of the dock receipt's arrival. (7) If the receiving broker believes that the cotton is unqualified within the validity period after delivery, they may request the convening of a standards appraisal meeting, which shall be convened by the exchange on a regular basis to compare the standards and judge them. If the product meets the standards, the appraisal fee shall be paid by the requester. If it is lower than the standard, it shall be borne by the exchange. The cotton appraisal fee is 70 silver yuan per 100 dan, 105 silver yuan for up to five times, and 140 silver yuan for up to ten times. (8) Jiangmaotian, Chuyongxing and Sanzhan were designated as cotton warehouses.

American Inflation Bill Passed 257

New York, April 26 - Weekly Cotton Market Situation: Raw cotton prices rose at the beginning of the week, but as urgent demand was met, the market showed a reactive sentiment and a tendency for profit-taking, which was further amplified when converting US dollars to British pounds. The debate in the Senate on the inflationary amendment to the rural relief bill caused some doubts about the final provisions of this plan. However, the authorities will clearly adopt measures to raise prices. Editor's note: According to recent news from Washington, the rural relief bill and its inflationary amendment have been passed by the Senate. News of a new cotton planting has been repeatedly delayed, and winter rainfall in the Southwest is lower than in the past, which can also be seen as an unfavorable factor for the future of cotton cultivation. Inflationary speculation has boosted demand for cotton, but cotton mills are only willing to sell futures for May or early June. There has been little change in the idea of cotton acreage. As for whether the rural relief bill can be implemented in time and affect cotton planting, this doubt is gradually increasing.

Silk and Tea - Spring Silkworms in Zhejiang Can Still Be Salvaged 258

(Shaoxing) In the villages, many silkworm farmers raised native breeds this year, but the weather was unfavorable, with continuous cold rain for weeks. The early batch of native silkworms almost suffered complete losses, but the late batch of foreign breeds has rarely been abandoned. Silkworm farmers in areas such as Lizhu, Wangtan, and Tangpu, knowing that mulberry trees produce leaves later, all raised improved breeds. After the silkworm eggs hatched, the weather turned sunny and warm, and the silkworms' development improved. The early batch has now reached the third molt, with uniform molting. The late batch in areas such as Anchang, Hengxi, and Tianle Township has also reached the second molt with abundant leaves, and the current situation is quite good.

(Anji) Although the silkworm season in various towns and villages is later than in Hangzhou, incubation began before the Grain Rain festival. This year, the weather has been severely cold, and mulberry trees are budding later, so the silkworm season is about half a month later than last year. Currently, the weather is sunny and warm, and mulberry leaves are gradually flourishing. Silkworm farmers, aware of the disadvantages of native silkworms in Hangzhou, are all raising improved breeds. Although the feeding volume is not smooth in areas such as Meixi and Dipu, foreign silkworms have hatched quite uniformly and are developing well due to the suitable climate. The early batch has been in dormancy for four or five days, and the late silkworms have also started feeding on trial leaves. If the weather does not change again, the spring silkworms in Zhejiang can still be salvaged.

Several News Items Regarding New Tea 259

Qimen Black Tea Begins Harvesting and Production

Qimen black tea, around this time last year, the tribute teas of various firms had already been harvested and dried. This year, the climate has been consistently cold, and the heavy rain for four days last week severely restricted the development of tea buds. Fortunately, the weather suddenly turned sunny and warm in the past two days, and the Mao Feng and Bai Mao varieties are just right for harvesting. Farmers in various mountains are preparing to take advantage of this sunny weather and open their gardens immediately. Harvesting has already begun on the southwest routes. The tea workers and buyers of the last batch of each firm have all gathered in recent days and are busily preparing to leave for the villages to start weighing and compete to collect the green leaves. With such consistently sunny and warm weather, the top-quality tribute teas will receive dew nourishment in the morning and benefit from drying in the sun during the day, so the product will definitely be excellent. Tea firms are delighted by this weather, and farmers, confident in the superior quality of their goods, are announcing that they will not sell cheaply. Currently, the main goal of the firms is to avoid repeating last year's high mountain prices and heavy losses. Regardless of the weather this year, they are unanimously determined not to undercut each other and drive up prices. With this approach, it remains to be seen whether prices can be lowered as desired.

Wuyuan Tea Market Gradually Shows Signs of Improvement

Recently, due to the sunny and warm weather, the buds of Zhouyuan tea in Wuyuan County have been growing longer. In previous years, farmers in various mountains would have already hired tea workers and gone to the market to buy goods and food, creating a bustling scene. Now, as the new tea is about to be harvested, poor farmers are unable to borrow money from merchants and cannot obtain goods on credit, and they have not yet purchased rice, oil, firewood, and other necessities. This state of distress is rarely seen. Among the tea firms in various villages, those with strong financial resources are already preparing to open their businesses, while those with depleted funds are still watching and waiting to regain their footing due to tightened credit from banks. In total, about 60% of the old and new tea firms in the villages have decided to open their businesses this year. The demand for various items used by tea firms, such as box boards, firewood, and charcoal, which have been neglected for a long time, is gradually increasing as the firms open their businesses, and orders are becoming more sought after. The livelihood of mountain farmers has thus been slightly eased. However, prices are still difficult to recover as sales are lower than in the past. Overall, the tea market has shown signs of improvement this week.

Xiaoshan Mao Tea Begins Weighing

The green tea in areas such as Xiaoshan, Zhuji, and Yuyao in Zhejiang Province has been in demand in recent years as local firms send personnel to compete for the purchase of tender tips and offer higher prices for selected leaves. As a result, tea farmers in various areas are all harvesting earlier. Yesterday, a tea factory received a letter from Xiaoshan stating that the new tea in that area had begun to be weighed, with a price of 68 yuan per dan. Those with superior quality are selling for 75 yuan.

Suian New Tea Arrives in Shanghai 260

Yesterday, the Chen Ji Tea Factory in Suian transported eight packages of new green tea to Shanghai. The results of brewing tests showed that the aroma and color were excellent. They will start production soon to meet the needs of foreign merchants.

Weekend Silk Market Remains Sluggish 261

There was nothing good to report in the silk market yesterday. Overseas prices were stable, but domestic demand was weak. Transactions totaled only 10 bales of Month-free silk at 850 yuan, 20 bales of San Tiao Wu coarse green striped silk at 830 yuan, and 5 bales of 83-degree even silk at 710 yuan. In the past two weeks, the highest New York price was 1.54 and the lowest was 1.22, a difference of 0.32, a gain of 26%. The highest US exchange rate was 21.375 and the lowest was 25.00, a difference of 3.75, a decrease of 17%. According to this observation, it seems that the price increase is due to the exchange rate decrease, and transactions should be quite smooth. However, firstly, exporters are afraid to take risks due to the unstable market; secondly, the previous price difference was too large, resulting in no transactions; now, the rising trend is just enough to bring buyers and sellers closer together, but it has not yet attracted many sellers; thirdly, new silk has not yet been thrown on the market, and the quality of the existing stock is poor; fourthly, consumer prices are still high, and sellers prefer to sell to foreign firms. Therefore, the number of transactions in this period is only about 1,000 bales. Appended below are overseas market prices (April 28):

Unprecedented Children's Music Broadcasting Competition in Shanghai 269

Regulations for the Children's Music Broadcasting Competition Jointly Organized by Yongsheng Radio Station, Children's Morning Post, and Hengsen Radio Station

In order to promote children's art and guide children's proper entertainment, this station has specially organized a children's music broadcasting competition. The detailed methods are listed below:

(1) Children's music is temporarily divided into (1) singing (such as singing operas, Kunqu operas, etc.) (2) stringed instruments (such as jinghu, erhu, sanxian, etc.) (3) wind instruments (such as flute, xiao, etc.) (4) Western instruments (such as bugle, harmonica, organ, viola, etc.). Each person can only participate in one category. Each person's broadcasting time is limited to five minutes. All musical instruments used must be provided by the broadcaster.

(2) This competition is tentatively limited to 400 children (Yongsheng and Hengsen radio stations will broadcast 200 children each). Any boy or girl child in this city under the age of 15 can participate. Registration starts on May 1st and ends on the 8th. Broadcasting will begin on the 12th.

(3) This association has designated five registration locations: (1) Yongsheng Radio Station, opposite the Sincere Department Store on Nanjing Road (2) Hengsen Radio Station, Baoanfang, Nanjing Road (3) Children's Morning Post, No. 280 Shandong Road (4) Children's Amusement Market, China National Products Company, Nanjing Road (5) Lili Local Products Company, intersection of Zhejiang Road and Tianjin Road

(4) All children participating in the competition must have a parent or adult responsible for taking them to and from the radio station.

(5) This association will assign numbers to the participating children, publish them in the newspaper in advance, and notify the participating children. They will be divided into days and periods and distributed evenly to the Yongsheng and Hengsen radio stations for broadcasting.

(6) Children's music broadcasting will be from May 12th to 22nd, broadcast twice a day. The first time will be on Yongsheng Radio Station, from 2:30 PM to 4:00 PM. The second time will be on Hengsen Radio Station, from 6:45 PM to 8:15 PM.

(7) This association will specially invite listeners to judge during the children's music program. In addition to printing the evaluation form in the Morning Post every day, it will also be distributed to specially invited critics. Anyone who loves children's art and is willing to be a judge can obtain it from the registration locations listed above.

(8) In order to encourage children's musical interest, this association has established the following award methods:

1. Ordinary Award: 400 people will each receive a commemorative art medal from this association.

2. Group Award: This association will select the top three in each of the four groups: singing, stringed instruments, wind instruments, and Western instruments, and give them group awards.

3. Special Award: The top 50 performers in each group will be given special awards. The top three in each group will receive special commemorative awards and have their photos taken for souvenir purposes.

(9) This association will also prepare awards to be given to listeners who provide criticism. All criticisms that match the top three winners (for example, if the top three winning numbers are 10, 20, and 30, then all criticisms that recognize 10, 20, and 30 as the winners) will be given awards by this association to express its appreciation.

(10) For the sake of serious criticism, this association will seal and preserve the daily evaluation forms from all listeners and periodically invite Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Yan Duhe, Zhou Shoujuan, Yan Esheng, Hu Shuyi, Xu Zhuodai, and Ding Song to open, compile, and verify them to determine the rankings, which will be published in the newspaper to promote this event.

Amateur Chat

Further Discussion on the Root Causes of China's Problems 270

— Pu

Since the issue of the location of the root causes of China's problems was published in the previous two issues of Amateur Chat, many readers have written to raise questions and request more detailed explanations. The content of the letters can be roughly divided into two categories:

(1) Why did the system collapse, and why did the culture disappear?

(2) They are eager to know the methods of remedy and the steps to be taken.

Regarding the first category of questions, a detailed explanation would have to include the ancient and modern Chinese history, which is beyond the capacity of this publication. Fortunately, we received a manuscript from Mr. Nie Zhi, which contains a passage that can be used as a concise answer to our explanation of the first category of questions. Its content is: "The current China is a semi-colonial China, an economically backward China. It is plagued by the shackles of international capitalist imperialism externally and suffers from the trampling of warlords and bureaucrats internally. The national economy cannot develop entirely because the lifelines of the country, such as customs, mines, factories, finance, and transportation, are directly or indirectly controlled by the hands of imperialism; and the internal economic organization collapses precisely because warlords and bureaucrats launch internal wars from time to time, freely increase exorbitant taxes and issue public bonds, and force the cultivation of opium and other acts of self-enrichment. In this environment riddled with holes, the success of the Chinese national liberation movement is definitely not the 'blood purchase' of a few high-ranking Chinese officials who want to preserve their titles; and for the sake of preserving their titles, they even put pressure on the uprising of the downtrodden lower-class people, as if they must be completely wiped out before they are satisfied! Facts speak louder than words. From the Qing government to the Beiyang warlords, and now to the present, there has been a consistent system that answers the riddle of 'I would rather give it to a friend than to a family slave'! Thus, the so-called 'integrity,' 'morality,' and 'duty' naturally ran into the land of nothingness. In the so-called land of Chinese civilization, the upper echelons 'sing praises and virtues' and have to act as 'talking parrots more poisonous than snakes'; the lower echelons 'scurry like dogs and operate like flies' and have to imitate the 'sending off the old and welcoming the new' prostitutes!"

In this situation, we can see the reasons for the collapse of the system and the crux of why a new culture cannot be produced.

When it comes to the issue of remedy, we deeply feel that although China's current symptoms are extremely dangerous, they are definitely not incurable. As long as more and more people in the country realize the danger, more and more people feel the pain, and the number of people who are prepared to spare no sacrifice to fight against imperialism externally and warlords and bureaucrats internally increases to a considerable extent, the day of national liberation will be near. We express our acceptance and satisfaction with all the questions raised by readers regarding the location of the root causes of China's problems. We, like the readers, feel that we must recognize the fundamental danger of our nation before we can determine the direction of our struggle and adopt more effective means. This abstract answer may still cause dissatisfaction among some readers, but in this era, being able to openly talk about these things is still considered fortunate!

Popular Literature and Art

The Typesetter 271

— Fang San

The room is dark and the lamp is dim, the lead characters are like black stars, standing in front of the frame all day long, legs aching like saws

Yesterday, eight hundred were typeset, today, a thousand are typeset, not minding the pain in the ten fingers, but fearing the deduction of wages

Ever since before sunrise, typesetting until after dusk, typesetting into a form, who will enjoy it

Suffering hardship year after year, living a hard life, why is it that the typesetter is not a scholar

Popular Life

The Flowers of a Bygone Era 272

— Ms. Liao Yinxiang

Flower Seller

Anyone who has been to Suzhou for sightseeing will probably have a slight impression of us! Every night around three o'clock, we go to the mountains together. Half of those engaged in this profession live near Mudu, but to pick fresh flowers, one must go to Tiger Hill, Tianping, or the Guanyin Temple in Qizi, as these mountains have different flowers. Therefore, we also pick flowers according to the season. Almost 360 days a year, there is always a flower to pick. From our residence to the nearest mountain, the furthest being about twenty li, if we go to pick them a bit late, we often can’t make it to the Suzhou morning market on time.

After picking the flowers, we return to Changmen in Suzhou—the place where our customers are concentrated—at the earliest around nine o'clock in the morning. As soon as we arrive at Changmen, many flower brokers are waiting. Two-thirds of these flowers are

Page 20

bought by them. If we take them to the flower stalls in the city, we won’t be able to sell them for much money. The remaining ones are taken by ourselves to various hotels to hawk. In the past one or two years, there were often times when there weren’t enough to sell, but in recent years, even if we sell until two or three o'clock in the afternoon, we still have a small half left. This isn’t because we aren’t willing to lower the price, but simply because there are too few buyers. At the latest, we must return by four o'clock. When we get home, we eat something and immediately go to sleep, otherwise, we won’t have enough energy for the next day. For lunch, we usually just bring some dry food to eat on the road. When business is good, we sometimes buy something to eat in Suzhou. We work for our food and clothing for what is said to be seventeen or eighteen hours, of which a large part of the time is spent on the road back and forth.

Engaging in this kind of business is remarkably hard. Not only is there often a lack of sleep, but also the daily long treks and the invasion of wind, frost, rain, and snow are not something that people without habit and training can endure. As a result, the money earned each day is barely enough to maintain my own life, and perhaps not even enough. Moreover, we have to give a portion to the hotel tea servers; otherwise, they will sabotage our transactions, and even not allow us to enter the hotel doors.

As for the mental suffering, it is even more unspeakable. Being bullied and humiliated is unavoidable every day; from the beginning of the transaction until we return home, we are constantly struggling in depression. Those young male flower brokers, hotel tea servers, and frivolous buyers often mock us, and even get physical. But no matter how embarrassing it is, we have to endure and smile obsequiously; otherwise, we will cut off our own means of making a living.

The fact that flower sellers are seduced or raped is constantly happening. As a result, many people like me unconsciously degenerate. Of course, most people who engage in this profession are not fortunate enough to receive education, but they have a deep understanding of and can put into practice the philosophical saying, "If not perfect, then rather nothing." Since our reputation is already ruined, and the stain on the white jade is irreparable, then why not sell ourselves happily? The material price obtained from selling oneself once exceeds the income from a month or more of hard work picking flowers, so we become actively willing after being passively forced. Some flower sellers also engage in prostitution, but for these people, selling flowers is only a side job. Every morning, they buy some flowers from us flower pickers to peddle. The reason they don't give up selling flowers is that it allows them to get to know more customers. Not only are they unwilling to engage in the hard work of picking flowers anymore, but they also don't have the time to go up the mountain in the middle of the night.

As for me? Fortunately, my father is the prompter in the X opera theater, and my mother is a predecessor in selling flowers, now engaged in miscellaneous jobs such as laundry in the X hotel. Therefore, some flower brokers and tea servers have old ties with us, and some I even have to call them "father's friends" as a sign of respect! Six years ago, when I was only twelve years old, I started selling flowers with my mother, so I am often seen as a child, and I rarely receive unbearable words or actions. Sometimes when some customers make things difficult for me, they come to my rescue. But even so, I have already suffered enough!

I remember that six years ago, this flower-selling business could barely be done, but in the recent year, judging by the number of flower pickers alone, there are only eleven or twelve people left, a reduction of about 70%. The number of flower sellers has also decreased by half. However, the supply of flowers always exceeds the demand, and the market downturn can be imagined. Therefore, for the sake of business, flower sellers often squeeze each other out, and many of them go to the city to do business with residents. And we flower pickers, now due to the sluggish business, even running to hotels is of no use. So we only pick flowers and often don’t sell them anymore, and the flower sellers are no longer the flower pickers. This is a big change that didn't exist before! However, we are not disappointed or pessimistic because of this. Let the flowers of the old era gradually wither away, but we believe that the flowers of the new era will bud and bloom from this point on. At that time, the various shackles that are locked on us will be transformed into beautiful garlands of victory, and we will also become "people" among the flowers!

People's Little Parliament

How Should Workers Maintain Their Livelihoods When Yarn Factories Reduce Work Case 273

— Proposer: Councilor Ms. Li Liumei

I am a female worker in the XX yarn factory. I can earn more than ten yuan a month, which is used to support my disabled old mother and myself, and I already feel that it is very insufficient. Now the manager says that because of the dumping of Japanese yarn, the factory's products are not selling well, and a decision has been made to reduce work. According to the reduced wages, I can only earn eight yuan a month, and the household expenses are even more insufficient. At that time, I discussed the ways to live in the future with several sisters. One sister said that people have been talking about boycotting Japanese goods since last year, so why can Japanese yarn still be dumped in our country now? This must be a trick by the manager to deal with us workers. Another sister said that starting yesterday, Japanese yarn factories have also reduced work. I asked her, since Japanese yarn has already been dumped in our country, why do they also need to reduce work? That sister said that the Japanese devils also say that yarn sales are not smooth! I was just about to say something, but before I could, one sister抢着(qiǎngzhe - interjected) said, if Chinese yarn factories reduce work and Japanese yarn factories also reduce work, then won't Chinese yarn factories have to reduce work even more? For the sake of making money, their domestic capitalists and foreign capitalists reduce work when you reduce work, they fight back and forth, but they don't care, but what about the lives of us workers? What about me, and my disabled fifty-four-year-old mother, how will we live?
